# UPSC Civil Services Main Examination

## GS Paper IV - Ethics, Integrity and Aptitude

### Model Answers (2018-2025)

---

*Source: Civilsdaily IAS*

---

## Question 1 (Year: 2022 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2022-gs4-q1-civilsdaily**

**2022 - It is believed that adherence to ethics in human actions would ensure the smooth functioning of an organization/system. If so, what does ethics seek to promote in human life? How do ethical values assist in the resolution of conflicts faced by him in his day-to-day functioning?** [Year: 2022] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

Ethics is a branch of philosophy that involves systematizing, defending, and recommending concepts of right and wrong conduct. It acts as a **‘moral compass’ **for individual and organisational conduct.

### Importance of Ethics in the Smooth Functioning of an Organization

1. Provides **Psychological Safety **which is essential for team efficiency. (Google’s **Project Aristotle)

2.** Stakeholder Loyalty- **attract and retain top talent, loyal customers, and stable investors.

3.** Conflict Prevention **by establishing clear behavioral norms.

4.** Risk Mitigation- **prevents scandals, lawsuits, and regulatory penalties. Eg- **Satyam Scandal**

5.** Brand Reputation- **Eg- Patagonia’s "Don't Buy This Jacket"campaign for mindful consumption

6.** Leadership **- "If ethics are poor at the top, that behavior is copied down through the organization." -

**Robert Noyce **(Intel Co-founder)

### Role of Ethics in human life

**1. The Realization of Human Dignity (Deontological Ethics) - **It promotes the inherent worth and "sacredness" of human life. Eg- **Abraham Lincoln’s **role in abolition of slavery

**2. Inner Peace and Psychological Well-being **by promoting "clear conscience" and reducing **cognitive dissonance. Eg- Gandhiji withdrawing NCM after Chauri Chaura.

3.** The Pursuit of the "Good Life" (Eudaimonia) - **helps individuals align their daily actions with their highest purpose.

**4.** Ethics provides a shared **"moral vocabulary" **needed for **social cohesion and harmony. **Eg- Values of tolerance and empathy

**5. Accountability and Responsibility - **Ethics encourages individuals to take ownership of their actions and their consequences. Eg- Lal Bahadur Shastri resigning after Rail accident

**6. Justice and Fairness - **Ethics seeks the equitable distribution of resources, opportunities, and burdens.

Eg- **Justice Ruth Bader Ginsburg’s **advocacy for gender equality

**7. Intellectual and Moral Growth **by promoting the habit of "The Examined Life."

**8. Compassion and Altruism - **It promotes "other-centeredness" and a sense of purpose for the giver.

Eg- Philanthropy by Aziz Premji

**Viktor Frankl’s Logotherapy, suggests that human life flourishes when we find a "Why" to live for

### Role of Ethical Values in Resolving Day-to-Day Conflicts

1.** Objectivity and Impartiality **helps address conflict of interest and promotes meritocracy.

2.** Integrity- **ensures consistency in thoughts, beliefs and actions thereby preventing **crisis of conscience.**

3.** Prioritization of values **- Eg- Choosing transparency over convenience under RTI.

4.** Empathy **and **Humility **allows an individual to listen and admit mistakes.

5.** Moral Courage **helps resolve "Fear vs. Duty" conflict. Eg- Satyendra Dubey exposing corruption in

Golden Quadrilateral project

6.** Managing Scarcity of Resources Fairly - Eg- Utilitarianism **guiding the “greatest good for the greatest number”

7. By adhering to a set of core values (Self-Alignment) an individual can reduce **Cognitive Dissonance.**

Thus, ethics provides both **direction and discipline **- it **guides what is right **and **strengthens the will to do it**

---

## Question 2 (Year: 2024 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2024-gs4-q2-civilsdaily**

**2024 - “Ethics encompasses several key dimensions that are crucial in guiding individuals and organizations towards morally responsible behaviour.” Explain the key dimensions of ethics that influence human actions. Discuss how these dimensions shape ethical decision-making in the professional context.** [Year: 2024] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

Ethics is a branch of philosophy that involves systematizing, defending, and recommending concepts of right and wrong conduct. It acts as a **‘moral compass’ **for individual and organisational conduct.

### Dimensions of Ethics Guiding Individuals

1.** Normative Ethics (The "Ought" Dimension)- **This is the **prescriptive side **of ethics. It includes

    a.** Deontology **(duty-based). Eg- Respecting human dignity

    b.** Utilitarianism **(consequence-based). Eg- guides policy for “greatest good for the greatest number”

2.** Meta-Ethics (The "Meaning" Dimension)- **It deals with the origin of moral principles. Helps solve dilemmas in emerging issues like AI ethics, ethics of biotechnology etc

3.** Descriptive Ethics (The "Observation" Dimension)- **It provides the empirical data on "what is" rather than "what should be."

4.** Virtue Ethics (The "Character" Dimension)- **helps in inculcating virtues like courage, honesty, and temperance. Eg- **Mahatma Gandhi **cultivated the virtue of Ahimsa as a personal habit.

5.** Applied Ethics **- Helps apply ethical principles in real life situations. Eg- Compassionate capitalism in corporate governance, Stewardship principle in environmental ethics.

6.** "Ethics of Care" - **emphasizes the importance of interpersonal relationships and compassion.

### Dimensions of Ethics Guiding Organizations

**1. The Justice Dimension **ensures fairness in both outcomes and processes.

- ** Distributive Justice- **Focuses on the fair allocation of rewards and burdens. Eg- Equal Remuneration Act

- ** Procedural Justice- **Ensures transparency and fairness in decision making.

**2. The Accountability Dimension - **promotes "fiduciary duty" towards stakeholders and prevents the "systemic rot" caused by secrecy. Eg-Infosys whistleblower policy

**3. The Sustainability and Stewardship Dimension **- Moving from a

"profit-only" model to the **Triple Bottom Line. Eg- IKEA’s "People & Planet Positive" strategy

4. Solving the **"Loyalty vs. Truth" dilemma **- the **Normative **dimension provides the duty to the truth, while the **Virtue **dimension provides the courage to speak it.

5. Builds **consistency, **predictability and smooth-functioning system based on stable, universal principles. Eg- Zomato’s menstrual leave policy

These dimensions ensure that human actions are not impulsive but reasoned. As **Jane Addams **said, "Action indeed is the sole medium of expression for ethics."

---

## Question 3 (Year: 2018 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2018-gs4-q3-civilsdaily**

**2018 - With regard to the morality of actions, one view is that means is of paramount importance and the other view is that the ends justify the means. Which view do you think is more appropriate? Justify your answer.** [Year: 2018] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

The debate between the "Ends" and the "Means" is one of the oldest in moral philosophy, representing the tension between **Consequentialism **(Teleology) and **Duty-based ethics **(Deontology).

### Justification of Ends (Consequentialism)

1.** Maximizing Welfare- **The primary goal is the "Common Good."

2.** Strategic Necessity- **Eg- For **realist scholars **of IR like **Morgenthau, national interest takes precedence over means

3.** Efficiency in Governance- **Eg- mandatory vaccination drives to address **vaccine hesitancy**

4.** Security and Intelligence- **surveillance or "white lies" are necessary to prevent terrorism.

5.** Scientific Progress- **Eg- Renaissance scientists stole bodies for dissection

6.** Economic Stabilization- **Eg- Governments used taxpayer money to save "Too Big to Fail" banks during 2008 crisis

7.** Crisis Management- **Eg- **Emergency Triage - **In war zones, doctors choose who to treat and who to let die based on survival probability

### Justification of Means (Deontology) - Immanuel Kant and Mahatma Gandhi

1.** Nishkama Karma (The Bhagavad Gita)- **humans are only in control of their actions (means), not the results (ends).

2.** Moral Integrity- **A "good" end achieved through "bad" means is a hollow victory that degrades the character of the actor.

3. As **Gandhi **famously said, "The means may be likened to a seed, the end to a tree."

4.** Protection of Individual Rights- **Deontology ensures that individuals are never treated as mere "tools" for a larger goal.

5.** Preventing the "Slippery Slope"- **Once you justify a small evil for a great good, it becomes easier to justify larger evils.

6.** Rule of Law- **A smooth-functioning society depends on everyone following the rules, even when it’s inconvenient.

7. Ensuring **accountability **- Eg- **Whistleblowing by Edward Snowden - **"end" (national security) did not justify the "means" (illegal mass surveillance and violation of privacy).

8.** Sustainable Peace- **Forced peace (ends) through war (means) rarely lasts. Eg- "Truth and

Reconciliation commission" in South Africa

### My View- I believe that the means are of paramount importance for the following reasons-

- Means are based on respect for **Human Dignity**

- ** Ends are Uncertain, Means are Absolute**

- ** The Character of the System **is defined by the culture and means used.

- ** Means build institutional trust**

---

## Question 4 (Year: 2020 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2020-gs4-q4-civilsdaily**

**2020 - Distinguish between laws and rules. Discuss the role of ethics in formulating them** [Year: 2020] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

While laws and rules serve as the structured framework to regulate conduct and ensure justice, ethics provides the mor foundation.

“Law is the minimum of morality.” - **Georg Jellinek**

### Objectives of Laws and Rules

1. Maintaining social order and stability.

2. Ensuring the safety and security of individuals.

3. Promoting fairness and equality.

4. Resolving conflicts.

5. Protecting the rights of the vulnerable.______________________________________________________

**Basis**
**Laws**
**Rules**

**Nature**
Formal legal enactments by legislature. Eg- DPDP Act, 2023
Subordinate instructions framed under law. Eg- DPDP rules, 2025

**Purpose**
Protect rights, order, and justice
Operationalise laws in daily functioning

**Authority**
Derived from Constitution and
Legislatures. Eg- RTI
Derived from delegated authority. Eg-CIC

**Scope**
Apply to entire society
Apply to specific organisations or contexts

**Enforceability**
Enforced by courts
Enforced administratively

**Flexibility**
Rigid and difficult to amend
More flexible

**Violation consequence**
Civil/criminal liability. Eg- Prison sentence
Disciplinary penalty. Eg- SEBI Fines

### Role of Ethics in Formulating Laws and Rules

1. Ethics acts as the **"internal monitor" **that ensures laws and rules do not become instruments of tyranny.

2.** Balancing rights and duties **of citizens. Eg- reasonable restrictions under **Article 19(2)**

3.** Providing a Moral Justification- **Eg- the law against theft is rooted in the ethical value of **respect for property.

4.** Upholding Human Dignity- **Eg- Protection of Civil Rights Act, 1955 to eliminate untouchability

5.** Ensuring Justice as Fairness (Rawls)- **Eg- 106th constitutional amendment Act for women reservation in parliament

6.** Promoting Transparency and accountability- **Eg- **RTI Act**

7. The ethical principle of **"Non-maleficence" **(do no harm) is the basis for environmental laws and safety regulations. Eg- EIA rules

8.** Professional Integrity- **Ethics informs "Codes of Conduct" in professions. Eg- the **Hippocratic Oath **for doctors

9.** Social welfare. Eg- MGNREGA guaranteeing employment.

Smooth functioning of any system depends on the synergy between ethics (to define the good) and laws/rules (to enforce the good).

---

## Question 5 (Year: 2023 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2023-gs4-q5-civilsdaily**

**2023 - Differentiate ‘moral intuition from ‘moral reasoning’ with suitable examples.** [Year: 2023] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**Ethical decision-making **is the process by which individuals evaluate options and make choices based on moral principles. It is **"dual-process" system **based on **emotional insight **(intuition) **and **rational evaluation (reasoning)**

| **Moral Intuition** | **Moral Reasoning** |

| --- | --- |

| Spontaneous, automatic moral response. | Deliberate, reflective moral evaluation. Eg- firing as a |

| Eg- firing in self defense | ‘last resort’ on violent Mob |

| Immediate. Occurs in millisecond | Slow. Requires time for reflection. |

| driven by "gut feelings." | Primarily cognitive |

| The process is hidden | logic can be explained to others. |

| Moves from "feeling" to "judgment." | Moves from "evidence" to "conclusion." |

| Based on emotions, empathy, social conditioning. Eg- prejudice towards Posititutes | Based on logic, ethical principles, critical thinking.
Eg- restricting movement of prostitutes due to Health concerns |

| --- | --- |

| Largely unconscious | Conscious and intentional |

| High Susceptibility to bias. | Low bias due to logical reasoning |

| Consistency may vary across situations and persons | More stable across similar cases |

| Useful for obvious wrongs | Necessary for complex conflicts |

**Examples**

**1. Moral Intuition**

    a.** The "Railway Track" Heroism by Nicholas Winton**

    b. The "Yuck" Factor in Bioethics

**2. Moral Reasoning**

    a. The Triage Decision in healthcare during crisis

    b. Kesavananda Bharati judgment - **Moral and Legal Reasoning **to develop the "Basic Structure Doctrine."

    c. Corporate Downsizing Decisions based on utilitarianism

**Moral Intuition **is the "Hero" who acts in the moment, while **Moral Reasoning **is the "Sage" who builds the system. Both are necessary for a morally complete life.

---

## Question 6 (Year: 2024 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2024-gs4-q6-civilsdaily**

**2024 - “The concept of Just and Unjust is contextual. What was just a year back, may turn out to be unjust in today’s context. Changing context should be constantly under scrutiny to prevent miscarriage of justice.” Examine the above statement with suitable examples.** [Year: 2024] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

In the words of John Rawls, "Justice is the first virtue of social institutions, as truth is of systems of thought." However, **Justice **is not a static or absolute concept but a dynamic one, shaped by the evolving moral, social, and technological landscape of a society.

**The Contextual Nature of Justice**

1.** Changing political contexts. **Eg- Colonial land laws once “legal”, now seen as exploitative.

2.** Changing economic contexts. **Eg- shift of policy focus from economic growth to inclusive growth

**3. Changing socio-cultural contexts. Eg- Sati **was socially accepted earlier but now a criminal offence.

**4. Changing technological contexts. **Eg- A decade ago, **mass data harvesting **was acceptable but now criticised for "Surveillance Capitalism" and violation **Privacy**

**5. Changing legal contexts. **Eg- basic structure doctrine or Due Process (Menka Gandhi) expanding FRs

**6. Changing environmental contexts. **Eg- shift from unlimited resource extraction to intergenerational justice

**7. Changing corporate governance contexts. **Eg- shift from **profit motive to TBL (people profit planet)**

### Need for Scrutiny to Prevent Miscarriage of Justice

1.** Avoiding "Legal Anachronism" **or **"Zombie Laws." **Eg- the decriminalization of Section 497

2.** Prevent legal injustice **- Laws may become oppressive if context changes. Eg- Sedition law

3. Non scrutiny leads to **moral stagnation. Eg- persistence of manual scavenging.

4. Adapting to **changing social realities. Eg- live in relationships or single parent families

5.** Maintain legitimacy **of state. Eg- RTI Act for transparency in governance

6. Protection of vulnerable sections. Eg- legal **recognition of Mental Health.**

7.** Preventing Technological Tyranny - Eg- Right to be Forgotten **under data protection Acts

8. As a society becomes more civilized, the **"just" methods of punishment **are needed. Eg- over 100

countries abolished Death penalty

9. Addressing **"New" Harms **in the Digital Age. Eg- AI generated **Deepfakes**

**10. To uphold constitutional morality. Eg- Triple talaq **invalidated despite social practice. “The Only Constant in Life Is Change.”- **Heraclitus**

Thus, Justice must be a **"living" **concept for human progress and **"Good Life" (Eudaimonia)**

---

## Question 7 (Year: 2021 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2021-gs4-q7-civilsdaily**

**2021 - “Integrity is a value that empowers the human being.” Justify with suitable illustration.** [Year: 2021] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

Integrity is the alignment of **Manasa (Thought), Vacha (Word), and Karmana (Action). **In the words of **C. S. Lewis, **“Integrity is doing the right thing even when no one is watching.”

### Role of integrity in empowers human being

### Empowerment at the Personal Level

1.** Inner Peace- **Integrity eliminates the **"cognitive dissonance" **and provides the mental energy needed to focus on goals.

2. Integrity ensures **predictability and reliability **in behavior - Key qualities of a **natural leader. **Eg- Mahatma Gandhi’s adherence to Ahimsa in personal life

3.** Integrity **acts as a foundation of genuine **self-esteem **and **confidence. Eg- Sanchin

Tendulkar refusing advertisement of Tobacco and Cigarettes brands.

### Empowerment at the Family Level

1. Parents with integrity empower children with a living blueprint of **"The Good Life".

2. Integrity creates an environment of **emotional safety **and **trust **within the family.

3. “The strength of a nation derives from the integrity of the home.” - **Confucius**

### Empowerment at the Social Level

1.** Builds Social Capital- **Integrity is the **"currency" **of social trust.

2.** Inspiration to Others **("ripple effect" of goodness). Eg- **Babasaheb Ambedkar **inspiring generations of Dalit leaders

3.** Catalyst for social change **- Eg- **Rosa Parks’s **refusal to give up her bus seat led to the Civil Rights Movement.

### Empowerment at the Professional Level

1.** Moral Courage- **the **“inner transparency” **empowers a person to speak truth to power. Eg- Satyendra Dubey

2. Integrity builds a **reputation **and **trust **that acts as a multiplier for one’s influence and opportunities. Eg-Metro man **E. Sreedharan**

3. Gives **moral authority **to lead. Eg- **Captain Vikram Batra **leading from the front in Kargil War.

4. Integrity helps in **objective decision making. **Eg- T. N. Session as CEC

5.** Knowledge without integrity is dangerous and dreadful. Eg- developing of Nuclear bomb

Thus, integrity provides **"oneness" **that builds character and ensures that actions are rooted in truth, justice, and dignity.

---

## Question 8 (Year: 2018 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2018-gs4-q8-civilsdaily**

**2018 - “In looking for people to hire, you look for three qualities- integrity, intelligence and energy. And if they do not have the first, the other two will kill you.” - Warren Buffett** [Year: 2018] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

Integrity without knowledge is weak and useless, and

knowledge without integrity is dangerous and dreadful -**Samuel Johnson**

1.** Intelligence + Energy - Integrity **= **DANGER .

2.** Integrity + Intelligence - Energy **= **STAGNATION**

3.** Integrity + Energy - Intelligence **= **INEFFICIENCY**

4.** All Three Combined **= **SUSTAINABLE LEADERSHIP.**

### Consequences of Intelligence and Energy

Without Integrity

1.** Sophisticated Fraud- **A smart individual can bypass internal controls and audit trails. Eg-**Bernie Madoff **running ponzi scheme.

2. High energy without integrity leads to **"winning at any cost," **resulting in a toxic **"cut-throat"**

culture that destroys team morale.

3.** Reputational damage- **Eg- manipulation of financial data to show "**paper profits,**" in **Enron case**

4.** Erosion of Stakeholder Trust - Eg- The NSE Co-location Case (Chitra Ramkrishna).**

5.** Systemic Exploitation **by finding loopholes in laws or company policies. Eg- Nirav Modi - PNB Fraud

6.** Corrosive Leadership- **"If ethics are poor at the top, that behavior is copied down through the organization." - **Robert Noyce **(Intel Co-founder)

7.** Legal risks- **Eg- **Subrata Roy’s (Sahara India) **massive "shadow banking" empire

8.** The "Smart Criminal" Effect- **intelligent and high energy do the wrong things faster and higher in scale. Eg- Harshad Metha

**On the other hand, integrity ensures**

1.** Moral Courage- **Eg- Satyendra Dubey

2. Integrity builds a **reputation **and **trust.. Eg- Metro man **E. Sreedharan**

3. Gives **moral authority **to lead. Eg- **Captain Vikram Batra **leading from the front in Kargil War.

4. Integrity helps in **objective decision making. **Eg- T. N. Session as CEC

5. Ensures adherence to Gandhian **“Trusteeship principle”**

Integrity is not an optional virtue but a necessary safeguard for **ethical corporate governance**

---

## Question 9 (Year: 2019 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2019-gs4-q9-civilsdaily**

**2019 - What is meant by the term ‘constitutional morality’? How does one uphold constitutional morality?** [Year: 2019] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**Constitutional morality **implies adherence to the **core principles and spirit **of the Constitution in a democracy. In the words of **Ambedkar, **“Constitutional morality is not a natural sentiment. It has to be cultivated”.

**George Grote, in his **History of Greece, **described constitutional morality as a **“rare and difficult sentiment” **involving

1. Paramount reverence for **forms and procedures **of the Constitution.

2. Adherence to law while enabling **open criticism **of authority.

3. Need for **public reason, self-restraint, and trust **in institutions.

### Other Pillars

1.** Rule of Law **- Eg- Article 14

2.** Institutional Integrity **- Eg- autonomy of EC, CAG

3.** Progressive Interpretation **- Eg- right to privacy

4.** Equality and Dignity **- Eg- Sabrimala Judgment

5.** Constitutional Values **- Upholding justice, liberty, equality, fraternity

6.** Separation of Powers **and **Checks and Balances**

**Upholding constitutional morality**

**1. By Judiciary**

- ** Prioritizing Constitutional over Social Morality- **Eg- Navtej Singh Johar case

- ** Protecting Dissent and Liberty- **Eg- upholding "Bail is the rule, Jail is the exception."

- ** Ensuring procedural fairness **- Following due process and natural justice.

**2. By Legislature**

- ** Debate and Deliberation- **Eg- mandatory referral of bill to Parliamentary committee (UK Model)

- ** Inclusive Law-making **to protect the interests of the marginalized. Eg- **Rights of Persons with Disabilities Act, 2016**

- **• Ensuring representation - **Eg- Nari Shakti Vandan Adhiniyam, 2023

- ** Social Reform through Legislation **to rectify historical injustices. Eg- Triple Talaq Act

**3. The Executive**

- ** Self-Restraint in Power- **Eg- Following the **S.R. Bommai guidelines **to avoid the unnecessary imposition of President’s Rule (Article 356).

- ** Adherence to the "Rule of Law"- **Eg- Strictly following the **D.K. Basu guidelines **to prevent custodial torture.

**4. Public Administration**

- ** Anonymity and Neutrality- **Providing "fair and fearless" advice to ministers

- ** Practicing Compassion- **Using "administrative discretion" to help the last person in the queue (Antyodaya). Eg- **S. Shankaran **in implementing the **Bonded Labour Abolition Act**

- ** Transparency and Honesty- **Proactive disclosure under the **RTI Act.

**5. By Citizens (The Sovereign)**

- ** Tolerance of Dissent- **Respecting the right of others to have a different opinion, religion, or lifestyle.

- ** Performing Fundamental Duties- **Recognizing that rights come with responsibilities (Article 51A).

- ** Active Participation- **Eg- Participating in **Gram Sabhas **or city ward committee meetings Constitutional morality serves as the **"North Star," **ensuring that the ship of the state remains anchored in the values of human dignity and social justice.

---

## Question 10 (Year: 2025 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2025-gs4-q10-civilsdaily**

**2025 - “Constitutional morality is not a natural sentiment but a product of civil education and adherence to the rule of law.” Examine the significance of constitutional morality for public servants highlighting the role in promoting good governance and ensuring accountability in public administration.** [Year: 2025] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**Constitutional morality **implies adherence to the **core principles and spirit **of the Constitution in a democracy.

**George Grote, in his **History of Greece, **described constitutional morality as a **“rare and difficult sentiment” **involving

4. Paramount reverence for **forms and procedures **of the Constitution.

5. Adherence to law while enabling **open criticism **of authority.

6. Need for **public reason, self-restraint, and trust **in institutions.

### Significance in Promoting Good Governance

1.** Promoting Transparency **- Open processes and access to information. Eg - **The "Jan Soochna**

**Portal" in Rajasthan**

2.** Ensuring Responsiveness **- CM treats the "Right to be Heard" as a fundamental right. Eg - grievance redressal through CPGRAMS

3.** Enhancing Effectiveness **- Decisions aligned with public interest. Eg- DBT via JAM trinity

4.** Fostering Participation **- Inclusion of stakeholders in decisions. **Eg- The Nagaland "Communitisation" of Public Services**

5.** Equity and inclusiveness **- Fair distribution of resources and opportunities. Eg- **Forest Rights Act**

6.** Consensus orientation **- Mediation and dialogue over coercion. Eg- **The GST Council**

7.** Strategic vision **- Long-term constitutional goals guide policy. Eg- Sustainable development.

**8. Rule of Law - **CM ensures that the law is applied impartially, preventing "Rule by Law." **Eg-Enforcement of the Model Code of Conduct (MCC)**

### Role in ensuring accountability

1.** Legal accountability **- Eg- Strictly following the **D.K. Basu guidelines **to prevent custodial torture.

2.** Political accountability **- Responsiveness to elected representatives within limits. Eg- Parliamentary questions.

3.** Social accountability **- Eg- **MGNREGA Social Audits in Andhra Pradesh.**

4.** Financial accountability **- Prudent and transparent use of public funds. Eg- **Audit of the 2G Spectrum and Coal Block Allocations.**

5.** Professional and Administrative Accountability - **CM ensures that the "Steel Frame" maintains institutional integrity. Eg- T. N. Seshan as CEC

6.** Future accountability **- promotes "Intergenerational Equity.” Eg- EIA norms

7.** Moral Accountability - **CM prevents the "Banalization of Evil," where officers claim they were "just following orders." **Eg- Whistleblowing in the Vyapam Scam.**

**8. Procedural accountability **- Following due process and natural justice.

### Challenges

1.** Conflict with Social Morality- **Eg- sabrimala

2.** Political Populism**

3.** Legacy of Colonial Laws- **Eg- Official Secrets Act

4.** Bureaucratic Inertia- **A "Status Quo" mindset

5.** Lack of Incentives- **Eg- "Yes-men" culture

6.** Weak Civil Education**

7.** The "Neutrality vs. Commitment" Dilemma**

Constitutional morality serves as the **"North Star," **ensuring that the ship of the state remains anchored in the values of human dignity and social justice.

---

## Question 11 (Year: 2020 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2020-gs4-q11-civilsdaily**

**2020 - Discuss the role of ethics and values in enhancing the following three major components of Comprehensive National Power (CNP) viz. human capital, soft power (culture and policies) and social harmony.** [Year: 2020] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

CNP is a **holistic measure **of a **nation's ability **to pursue its strategic objectives. It includes

**1. "Hard" dimensions **- military, economy, territory

**2. "Soft" dimensions **- culture, governance, social cohesion.

### Role of ethics and values in enhancing CNP

**Human Capital**

1.** Integrity in the education system **prevents systemic corruption like paper leaks or degree fraud.

2. Values like **punctuality **and **"Dharma" **increase **productivity. Eg- Japanese concept of **"Kaizen"**

3. Ethics promotes **meritocracy **by ensuring fairness in recruitment - prevents **"Brain Drain"**

4. Creating a **healthy and resilient population **- Values ensure that medical professionals **prioritize patient care **over commercial gain.

5. Values of **gender equality and respect **unlock 50% of the nation’s latent human capital.

6.** The trusteeship model **encourages "Giving Back" through CSR or philanthropy. Eg- **Tata Group**

### Soft Power

1.** Cultural diplomacy - Yoga and Ayurveda, rooted in the value of holistic well-being, have become India's most successful soft-power exports.

2. Values of **tolerance and pluralism **projects **diversity as strength.**

3.** Ethics provides moral authority in foreign policy- **Eg- India’s **"Vaccine Maitri" **based on philosophy of "Vasudhaiva Kutumbakam".

4. Values of **peaceful co-existence **make a nation a **"benign power." **Eg- India’s history of **Non-Alignment **and "No First Use" nuclear policy.

5. India’s lead in the **International Solar Alliance **reflects a moral commitment to the planet (Prakriti) and **environmental stewardship.

6.** Humanitarian Assistance- **Eg- **Operation SamudraBandhu **(Sri Lanka Cyclones) showcased India as a "First Responder".

7.** Democratic values **enhance global image. Eg- Free and fair elections in India.

### Social Harmony

1.** Secularism and Tolerance **prevents communal conflicts. Eg- **Syncretic "Ganga-Jamuni Tehzeeb"**

2. A sense of **fraternity (Article 51A) **ensures that citizens support each other during crises.

3. When the marginalized feel the system is **"just and fair," **they are less likely to lean toward radicalism or insurgency. Eg- hearts and minds strategy in J&K

4. Values of **"Antyodaya" **ensure that economic growth is inclusive. Eg- PM KISAN Scheme

5. High **mutual trust **among citizens builds **social capital.**

6.** Conflict Resolution through Dialogue- **Eg- **peaceful resolution of the Ram Janmabhoomi **issue

### Challenges

1.** Erosion of Integrity- **Eg- politician-bureaucrat-corporate nexus (Vohra committee)

2.** Hyper-Nationalism vs. Global Values**

3.** Digital Disruption- **Eg- "Fake News" and hate speech

4.** Inequality- **1% owning 41% wealth (Oxfam)

5.** Crisis of Character- **"Banalization of Evil"

By harmonizing its ancient wisdom (Ahimsa, Satya, Asteya) with modern constitutional values (Justice, Liberty, Equality), India can become a **Vishwaguru**

---

## Question 12 (Year: 2020 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2020-gs4-q12-civilsdaily**

**2020 - “Education is not an injunction, it is an effective and pervasive tool for all round development of an individual and social transformation”. Examine the New Education Policy, 2020 (NEP, 2020) in light of the above statement.** [Year: 2020] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

"Education is the manifestation of perfection already in man." - **Swami Vivekananda**

Education goes beyond instruction. It is a **transformative force **shaping character, capability, and societal progress.

### Education as a tool for all-round development of an individual

1.** Cognitive Agility- **Develops critical thinking and problem-solving skills

2.** Emotional Resilience- **Fosters self-awareness and empathy

3.** Ethical Moorings- **Instills values like integrity and compassion

4.** Physical and Aesthetic Growth **through sports

5.** Vocational Dignity- **fosters a "dignity of labor" and life-skills.

6.** Social Intelligence- **Schools act as "mini-societies"

### Education as a tool for social transformation

1.** Social mobility- **acts as the "great leveler"

2.** Promotion of Secularism and Tolerance**

3.** Promotes democratic participation and ‘informed citizenry’**

4.** Gender Equality- **Eg- "Beti Bachao Beti Padhao" movement

5.** Develops scientific temper **and **critical thinking**

6. Acts as a **change catalyst. **Eg- rising **‘working women’**

### NEP 2020- Empowering Individual and Society

1.** Holistic Individual Growth **through **5+3+3+4 Structure **and Activity-based learning in Anganwadis

2.** Builds character through value Education- **integrates "Constitutional Values" (like Seva, Ahimsa, and Environmental conservation) into the curriculum.

3.** Promotes Multidisciplinary Learning- **Eg- Arts-science integration.

4.** Flexibility and Multiple Entry/Exit Options **through "Academic Bank of Credits" (ABC) ensures that individuals aren't punished for life interruptions.

5.** Vocational Integration **from Class 6 promotes **dignity of labor**

6.** Linguistic Empowerment **through 3 language formula bridges the gap between home and school

7.** Equitable Social Transformation - **Eg- **Gender Inclusion Fund **increases retention of girl students.

8. Ensuring **accessibility through Special Education Zones (SEZs) **in "Aspirational Districts"

9.** Technological Democratization- **The National Educational Technology Forum (NETF) aims to use AI and digital tools to reach the "last mile."

10.** Teacher Empowerment- **Eg- **NISHTHA **program to train teachers in innovative, learner-centric methodologies.

### Challenges in Implementation

1.** Low funding- **stagnant at **4.6% of GDP **(target of **6% of GDP)

2.** Digital Divide- **Eg- **digital apartheid **in rural India

3.** Logistics of Multilingualism- **Challenge in creating textbooks in **22+ regional languages**

4.** Federal issue - **Eg- TN opposition to **3-language formula**

5. Challenges in **mindset shift from rote to competency.**

Effective implementation of NEP can turn India into a **Global Knowledge Superpower **(Vishwaguru)

---

## Question 13 (Year: 2020 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2020-gs4-q13-civilsdaily**

**2020 - “The current internet expansion has instilled a different set of cultural values which are often in conflict with traditional values.’ Discuss.** [Year: 2020] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

As per **ITU, **over **6 billion **people globally and over **86% of households in India **use the internet. This expansion of the internet has acted as a **double-edged sword.**

**Emergence of New Cultural Norms in Conflict with Traditional Norms**

1.** Individualism vs. Collectivism - **Eg- emergence of nuclear families and single parent parent families replacing joint families

2.** Instant Gratification vs. Patience (Tapas) - **Eg- rise in **"Speed-Dating" apps **and "Swipe Culture" conflicting with traditional marriage systems

3.** Egalitarianism vs. Seniority - **Youth questioning traditional family hierarchies or social structures based on information found online. **Eg- **rise in inter caste marriages

4.** Transparency vs. Discretion - Eg- **culture of "oversharing" personal lives (Eg- vlogging) conflicts with traditional value of "keeping family matters private"

5.** Global vs. Ethnic Identity - **Eg- dilution of local linguistic dialects and regional folk songs in favor of "standardized" global pop culture.

6.** Fluid vs. Fixed Identity - **fluid "career hopping" encouraged by the internet is seen as "instability" by traditionalists who value life-long commitment.

7.** Materialism vs. Contentment - **constant consumption and luxury displays in conflict with traditional values of simple living and **“santosh.” **Eg- "FOMO" (Fear of Missing Out) marketing.

8.** Digital Nomadism vs. Rootedness - **weakening of local community bonds due to high mobility among youth.

9.** Crowd Wisdom vs. Institutional Expertise - Eg- **diagnosing health issues via "Dr. Google" or Reddit threads instead of certified doctors

10.** Moral Relativism vs. Absolute Codes. Eg- rising **social tension regarding traditional views on gender roles, and diet.

### Counter-Argument- Internet expansion strengthening traditional values.

1. Internet-driven **"Wellness Culture" **has expanded reach of Yoga and Ayurveda

2.** Linguistic conservation. Eg- **"People’s Linguistic Survey of India" **use digital recording to preserve tribal dialects like Santhali or Tulu

3.** Market Access for Traditional Artisans **- Eg- Platforms like **Etsy, Okhai, or GoCoop **allow Kalamkari artists to sell directly to global markets

4.** Live Streaming of temple Aartis (like Kashi Vishwanath) **allows virtual religious participation.

5. Food bloggers and YouTube channels focused on **"Village Cooking" **have documented rare regional culinary techniques. Eg- Village Food Factory

6. Modernizing Traditional Education. Eg- Vedic Math courses on Ed-tech

7.** Social Media as a Tool for "Cultural Assertion" - Eg- **Trends like **#SareeTwitter or #DhotiChallenge**

8. Emerging digital **"Sustainability" values **align with ancient traditional concepts of minimal living. Eg-**“slow fashion” **brands like **Ka Sha**

The emergence of **‘glocalization’ **represents the fusion of internet driven modernity and community-oriented wisdom of tradition.

---

## Question 14 (Year: 2024 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2024-gs4-q14-civilsdaily**

**2024 - The soul of the new law, Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita (BNS) is Justice, Equality and Impartiality based on Indian culture and ethos. Discuss this in the light of a major shift from a doctrine of punishment to justice in the present judicial system.** [Year: 2024] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

While the colonial **IPC **was designed by the British to **"rule and punish", the BNS is based on Indian ethos of Dharma and Nyaya to **"serve and provide justice" **to citizens.

**Soul of BNS**

### Justice (Nyaya)

1.** Victim Centrality- **For the first time, the victim has a say in the withdrawal of cases.

2.** Justice for vulnerable groups. Eg- Stringent punishment for rape and child abuse

3.** Mandatory timelines **for filing charge sheets and delivering judgments to prevent "justice delayed is justice denied.”

### Equality (Samata)

1. Providing **equal protection of law. **Eg- Section 103(2) penalizes **Mob Lynching**

2.** Gender Inclusivity- **expands the definition of "gender" to include **transgender individuals**

3.** Gender equality. Eg- Uniform Age of Consent

### Impartiality (Nishpakshta)

1.** Digitization of Evidence- **Eg-Mandating videography of search and seizure operations

2.** Zero FIR- **Allows a citizen to file a complaint at any police station regardless of jurisdiction

3.** Scientific Investigation- **Shifts the focus from "police testimony" to "forensic truth."

4.** Accountability of Public Servants- **Eg- "deemed sanction" if the government fails to respond to a request within 120 days.

### Shift from Doctrine of Punishment to Justice

1.** From Ruler’s Law to Citizen’s Law- **IPC was for the British to rule India, BNS is for Indians to govern themselves.

2.** Restorative Punishment- **Section 4(f) introduces **Community Service **for the first time.

3. In the BNS structure, **"Offenses against the Human Body**" are moved to the beginning of the code, signaling that **human life **is more valuable than property rights.

4. Focus on **liberty and privacy **- Eg- Deletion of Adultery (Section 497 IPC) and Section 377

5.** Proportionality **- Punishment calibrated to gravity of offence. Eg- **Reduced punishment scales **for minor offences

6.** Victim-centric justice **- Eg- **Expanded victim compensation framework **under section 396

7. Removing **colonial laws. Eg- Repeal of Sedition

8.** Procedural fairness **- Emphasis on due process and natural justice.

9.** Simplification- **Reducing 511 sections to 358.

10.** Protection of dignity **- Eg- **Redefinition of sexual offences **in gender-neutral and victim-protective language.

11.** Moral Healing (Prayaschit)- **upholds Indian ethos of atonement rather than eternal stigmatization of the offender.

12.** Balance between deterrence and justice **- Eg- **Death penalty retained only for rarest of rare offences**

This reorientation strengthens the **ethical legitimacy and effectiveness **of India’s criminal justice system.

---

## Question 15 (Year: 2025 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2025-gs4-q15-civilsdaily**

**2025 - In the present digital age, social media has revolutionised our way of communication and interaction. However, it has raised several ethical issues and challenges. Describe the key ethical dilemmas in this regard.** [Year: 2025] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

Over **6 Billion **people worldwide and **491 million **people in India use social media. However, this expansion of

social media has acted as a **double-edged sword.**

### Social Media Revolutionizing Communication and Interaction

1.** Elimination of Geographical Barriers- **Platforms like WhatsApp and Zoom have turned the world into a "Global Village".

2.** Shift from Passive to Active Participation- **allows users to be **"Prosumers” **(consumers and creators of content)

3.** Democratization of Voice- **Eg- **#BlackLivesMatter **or **#MeToo **movements

4. The rise of Emojis, GIFs, and Memes has created a new **universal "digital dialect" **that conveys emotion more quickly than text.

5.** Civic and Political Engagement- **Eg- leaders using X for communication

### Ethical Issues and Challenges

1.** Privacy and Surveillance challenge- **Eg- the **Cambridge Analytica **scandal.

2.** Spread of Misinformation- **The "viral" nature of social media allows

"Fake News" to spread six times faster than the truth. ie6 Rise in Cybersecurity Incidents in India (2022-2024) 2q^

3.** Algorithmic Echo Chambers **creating polarized "digital silos". **(India**

**Hate Lab report) M**

4.** Cognitive Warfare- **Eg- "Bot-farms" to build anti-India narratives

5.** Cyber Stalking and Harassment - Eg- Women targeted through doxxing and revenge porn.**

6.** Digital Addiction- **Eg- "Infinite Scroll" syndrome **2022 2023 2024**

7.** Post Truth world- **Eg- **Deepfakes **make it difficult to distinguish between reality and fabrication.

### Key ethical dilemmas in social media

1.** Freedom of Speech vs. Content Moderation- **Balancing an individual's right to speak against the community’s right to be protected from hate speech.

2.** Privacy vs. Profit- **The tension between protecting user data and the platform's need for targeted advertising revenue.

3.** Connectivity vs. Isolation- **The paradox of being "connected" to thousands online while feeling deeply isolated in the physical world.

4.** Accountability vs. Anonymity- **Anonymity protects whistleblowers but also shields those who commit harassment without consequence. Eg- rise of **"Deepfake Extortion"**

5.** Authenticity vs. Curation- **The pressure to present an "idealized self" online versus the ethical value of being true to one's real-life identity.

6.** Information Accessibility vs. Intellectual Property- **The ease of sharing leads to dilemmas regarding "Plagiarism" and the loss of revenue for original creators.

7.** Democratization vs. Polarization- **While everyone has a voice, algorithms often push people into **"Filter Bubbles" **and **"Echo Chambers".

8.** Algorithmic Bias vs. Social Justice **- Eg- recruitment algorithms on major professional networking sites were **less likely to show high-paying technical job ads **to women

9.** Accuracy vs. Speed (The Viral Trap) - **In the "attention economy," being the first to break a story is rewarded with "reach," while slow fact-checking is penalized by the algorithm.

Social media is an **ethically "grey" space. A robust framework of **"Digital Ethics"**is needed to cultivate

**"Digital Mindfulness."**

---

## Question 16 (Year: 2018 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2018-gs4-q16-civilsdaily**

**2018 - Suppose the Government of India is thinking of constructing a dam in a mountain valley bond by forests and inhabited by ethnic communities. What rational policy should it resort to in dealing with unforeseen contingencies** [Year: 2018] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

India is one of the top 10 mega diverse countries of the world (8.1% of the world's species). A rational policy for dam construction must adopt a **dynamic risk-management framework.**

"Forests are the lungs of our land. A nation that destroys it destroys itself.." - **Franklin D. Roosevelt**

### Possible unforeseen contingencies

1.** Ecological degradation **- Submergence of forests and biodiversity loss.

2.** Cultural erosion **- Eg- loss of "Sacred Groves"

3.** Livelihood disruption **- Loss of agriculture, fishing, forest-based economy.

4.** Downstream ecological impact **- Eg- Altered river flow affecting agriculture and wetlands.

5.** Reservoir-induced seismicity **- Eg- **1967 Koyna Earthquake.

6.** Waterlogging and salinisation **causing soil degradation.

7.** Health risks **- Stagnant water increasing vector-borne diseases. Eg- Malaria and dengue

8.** Social conflict **- Tensions between locals, migrants, and authorities.

9.** Climate uncertainty **- Eg- Irregular monsoon impacting reservoir levels.

**Rational Policy for Dealing with Unforeseen Contingencies - **must be **Adaptive, Transparent, and Restorative.

1.** Comprehensive impact assessments **for **Procedural Justice**

    a. Integrated **Environmental, Social and Cultural Impact Assessments.

    b.** Adaptive management- **mandatory periodic reassessments every 5 years.

2.** The "Precautionary Principle"- **If a risk (like a GLOF) is scientifically plausible but uncertain, the policy must favor environmental safety over construction.

3. Ensuring **Free, Prior, and Informed Consent (FPIC) **by Gram Sabhas under **PESA Act 1996.

4.** The "Benefit-Sharing" Model- Making communities "partners in prosperity."**

    a.** Just and participatory rehabilitation - **Eg- Land for land

    b.** Ecological Insurance Fund **from electricity revenue for unforeseen disaster relief.

    c.** Tribal Development Fund **for **Livelihood for Life**

5.** Cultural Heritage Mapping **before submergence.

6.** Ecological offsets **- Compensatory afforestation and biodiversity corridors. (Inter-generational Equity principle)

7.** Grievance Redressal at the Doorstep **through an independent **Project Ombudsman.

8.** Risk governance **- Eg- Flood warning systems downstream.

9.** Decommissioning Clause- **a clear "End-of-Life" plan for the dam, ensuring the valley can eventually be restored.

"Development without Justice is merely organized plunder." By treating the mountain ecosystem with **"Bio-centric Humility," **the state can mitigate the moral and physical risks of development.

---

## Question 17 (Year: 2024 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2024-gs4-q17-civilsdaily**

**2024 - Global warming and climate change are the outcomes of human greed in the name of development, indicating the direction in which extinction of organisms including human beings is heading towards loss of life on Earth. How do you put an end to this to protect life and bring equilibrium between the society and the environment?** [Year: 2024] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

The crisis of climate change is fundamentally a **crisis of values. It is the product of pursuing **material progress **by disregarding **planetary boundaries.

"Earth provides enough to satisfy every man's needs, but not every man's greed." - **Mahatma**

**Gandhi**

| **Human Greed** | **Ecological & Biological Impact** |

| --- | --- |

| **Fossil Fuel addiction** | Massive CO2 emissions (38.1 billion tonnes **in 2025) |

| **Deforestation for development** | Habitat loss for 80% of terrestrial species. |

| **Industrial Agriculture** | Soil degradation and the "insect apocalypse" |

| **Fast Fashion & Consumerism** | microplastic pollution |

| **Illegal Wildlife Trade** | increased risk of zoonotic pandemics. |

| **Overfishing** | Collapse of marine biodiversity and "dead zones" |

| **Urban Sprawl** | Heat island effects |

**Ways to Bring Equilibrium Between Society and Environment**

**Global Level- Systemic Harmonization**

- ** Decarbonization of Global Trade-**

Eg- taxing products imported from high-pollution regions

- ** Climate Finance Mobilization**Fulfilling the $100 billion annual commitment by developed countries

- ** Protection of global commons **- Eg-early finalization of Global Plastic Treaty to protect oceans **Government Level- act as the "Architect of Sustainability"**

- ** Rights of Nature Legislation-**

Formally granting legal personhood to

major rivers, mountains, and forests. Eg- Ganga in india

- ** Energy Transition **under **Panchamrit Targets- 500 GW **from non-fossil sources by 2030.

- ** Green Urban Planning- **Developing "Sponge Cities" with permeable pavements and urban wetlands to manage flooding and "Heat Island" effects.

### Business Level

- ** Adopting Net-Zero Roadmaps- **Measuring and reducing **Scope 1, 2, and 3 emissions**

- ** Product Stewardship- **Designing products that can be easily repaired or recycled

- ** ESG Integration **in investment decisions, recognizing that "Sustainability is a Competitive Advantage."

- ** Supply Chain Decarbonization- **ensuring that raw materials are sourced ethically and without deforestation.

- ** Bio-Inclusive Boardrooms- **Eg- "Ecological Representative" or "Voice for Future Generations" on corporate boards

### Society Level- Cultural Re-engineering

- ** Mainstreaming "Environmentalism of the Poor"- **Eg- **Chipko **or **Appico movements **where local tribes are the primary guardians of forests.

- Moving from "Environmental Science" to **"Environmental Ethics" **in school **and college curricula**

- ** Community-Led Restoration- **Eg- volunteer movements for cleaning coastlines or planting "Miyawaki" urban forests.

### Citizen Level- LiFE (Lifestyle for Environment) movement

- ** Mindful Consumption **through **ethical restraint**

    a. Switching from a "throwaway culture" to one of repair and reuse

    b. lifestyle of **"Enoughness"**-voluntarily limiting consumption

    c.** "Pro-Planet" **dietary Shift to protect water and soil. Eg- millet-based diets

- ** Energy Citizenship- **Transitioning to rooftop solar and adopting energy-efficient appliances (LEDs/BLDC fans).

- ** Waste Segregation at Source- **helps 100% composting or recycling at the municipal level.

- ** Green Mobility- **Preferring public transport, cycling, or Electric Vehicles (EVs)

By applying the **Precautionary Principle **to our technology and **Intergenerational Equity **to our economy, we can move to the trajectory of **"Great Restoration."**

---

## Question 18 (Year: 2025 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2025-gs4-q18-civilsdaily**

**2025 - Keeping the national security in mind, examine the ethical dilemmas related to controversies over environmental clearance of development projects in ecologically sensitive border areas in the country.** [Year: 2025] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

While national security is a **non-negotiable sovereign duty, ecological health is a **non-negotiable biological necessity. The ethical dilemma arises because both sides claim the "Right to Life" (Article 21).

### National security imperative

1.** All weather connectivity. **Eg- **Zojila **or **Sela tunnels**

2.** Logistics and supply lines**

3.** Surveillance and communication. **Eg- Installing radar stations

4.** Rapid deployment capability**

5.** Strategic deterrence. **Eg- Great Nicobar Port in IOR

6.** Disaster response access**

7.** Hearts and minds strategy. Eg- vibrant village program

### Ethical dilemmas related to environmental clearance

1.** Utilitarianism vs. Deontology/ right vs right dilemma - **sacrificing a unique, irreplaceable ecosystem for the "greater good" of national security.

2.** Connectivity vs ecology **- Highway projects degrade fragile ecosystems. Eg- Char Dham Pariyojana

3.** Anthropocentrism vs. Ecocentrism- **Does a border road have more "value" than the extinction of an endemic species?

4.** National interest vs local rights **- Eg- **Forest Conservation (Amendment) Act 2023 **exempts projects within 100km of borders from certain clearances.

5.** Speed vs scrutiny **- Eg- Strategic exemptions from EIA.

6.** Secrecy vs transparency **- Classified projects limit public accountability.

7.** Intergenerational justice dilemma **- Immediate defence gains create long-term ecological vulnerability. Eg- Landslides due to hill cutting.

8.** Human safety vs wildlife protection **- Eg- Border fencing affecting elephant movement.

9.** Development vs sustainability **- Infrastructure improves access but undermines long-term ecological balance.

10. Slippery Slope dilemma - extension of ‘national security exemptions’ to other projects in future

Case studies

1.** Great Nicobar Project - **Loss of **130 sq. km of rainforest**

2.** Arunachal Frontier Highway - **Fragmentation of the **Dibang Valley**

3.** Zojila Tunnel - **Disruption of **permafrost and glacial hydrology**

### Way Forward

- ** Strategic Environmental Assessment (SEA)**

- ** Green Engineering. Eg- **"Eco-bridges"

- ** Independent Oversight Body **comprising both military strategists and ecologists

- ** Restorative Compensation**

There is need to shift from "Environmental Clearance" to **"Environmental Integration" **for sustainable and **"Sensitive” security **paradigm.

---

## Question 19 (Year: 2020 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2020-gs4-q19-civilsdaily**

**2020 - “The will to power exists, but it can be tamed and be guided by rationality and principles of moral duty.’ Examine this statement in the context of international relations.** [Year: 2020] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

The statement represents the “2nd great debate” in International Relations between **Realism **and **Liberalism/Idealism.

### The "Will to Power"- The Realist Foundation

1.** Human Nature- **humans (and by extension, states) have an innate **animus dominandi**-a lust for power. (Hans Morgenthau.)

2.** Anarchy- **In an international system with no global government, states must seek power to ensure their **surviva**l.

3.** Zero-Sum Game- **if one state gains power, another feels less secure, leading to the **"Security Dilemma." **Eg- Pakistan’s nuclear tests after India

4.** Hegemonic Ambition- **Eg- **China’s "Global Civilization Initiative"**

5.** Territorial Expansionism- **Eg- **Russia’s ongoing annexation of Ukrainian territories**

6.** Nuclear Proliferation **for deterrence and prestige. Eg- **North Korea and Iran**

7.** Technological Supremacy- **Eg- **U.S.-China "Chip War" (2025)**

8.** Resource Weaponization- **Eg- **OPEC+ production cuts **in late 2024

### Taming through "Rationality"- The Neoliberal Approach

1. Rationality suggests that **cooperation provides better long-term outcomes **than conflict.

2.** Interdependence- **Trade creates "mutual destruction" risks that make peace more logical. Eg-U.S.-China trade

3.** International Institutions- **bodies like the UN, WTO, and IMF provide a framework for negotiation.

4.** Regime Theory- **It is easier to follow a shared rule than to fight for dominance every time a dispute arises.

5.** Standardization of Global Tech- **Eg- The **Global AI Safety Summit (2025)**

6.** Collective Security- **Eg- **Sweden and Finland’s 2024-25 integration into NATO**

### Guiding by "Principles of Moral Duty"- The Constructivist and Liberal View

1. IR is not just about cold logic, but about **Norms, Ethics, and Identity.**

2.** Democratic Peace Theory- **"moral duty" toward democratic values prevents democracies from going to war with one another.

3.** Human Rights- **"will to power" (state sovereignty) is tamed by the moral duty to prevent mass atrocities. Eg- **Responsibility to Protect (R2P) **doctrine

4.** Constructivism- **Thinkers like Alexander Wendt argue that "anarchy is what states make of it." If states adopt a "Kantian" philosophy, the will to power is replaced by a **will to cooperate.**

5.** The "Nuclear Taboo"- **Eg- The **G20 2024 New Delhi Declaration **reiterating that "the use or threat of nuclear weapons is inadmissible."

6.** Human Rights Advocacy- **Eg- **ICC arrest warrants (2024-25) **for leaders accused of war crimes

### Challenges

1.** The Return of Geopolitics- **Eg- Russia-Ukraine conflict and tensions in the South China Sea

2. Rise of **protectionism and territorial nationalism.**

**3. Erosion of Multilateralism. **Eg- crisis of credibility of UN

4. Asymmetric warfare. Eg- state sponsored terrorism.

The statement is an appeal for **Enlightened Realism **through the "rational" design of institutions and a shared "moral" commitment to human dignity

---

## Question 20 (Year: 2021 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2021-gs4-q20-civilsdaily**

**2021 - “Refugees should not be turned back to the country where they would face persecution or human right violation.” Examine the statement with reference to ethical dimension being violated by the nation claiming to be democratic with open society.** [Year: 2021] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

Violation of **principle of non-refoulement **creates a **"Liberal Paradox," **where the values used to define the state are discarded at its borders.

### Refugee Rights

1.** Right to Asylum **(Article 14 of the UDHR).

2.** Right to Life and Liberty**

3.** Right to Non-Discrimination**

4.** Freedom from Torture**

5.** Right to Due Process**

6.** Family unity**

7.** Access to basic services**

### Ethical Dimensions Violated by Refoulement

1.** Violation of Kantian Categorical imperative- **treats refugees as mere "means" to a political end border security.

2. Violation of **Justice as Fairness (John Rawls) **by sending refugees to face **persecution or human right violation**

3.** Breach of Universal **values like liberty, right to life. Eg- Alyan Kurdi death

4.** Erosion of Human Dignity **and an active denial of their **Intrinsic Worth. Eg- Detention camps for asylum seekers.

5.** Loss of moral leadership **and **global solidarity**- Undermines credibility in human rights advocacy

6.** Erosion of rule of law **- Ignoring international refugee conventions. Eg- Violations of 1951 Refugee Convention.

7.** Failure of the "Good Samaritan" Principle **i.e. preventing great harm (death) with comparatively small cost.

8.** Failure of humanitarian duty **- Moral obligation to protect the vulnerable is ignored.

9.** Discrimination **- Selective hospitality based on race, religion, or politics. Eg- Preferential treatment of Ukrainian refugees over African refugees in Europe.

10.** Epistemic Injustice- **Refusing to believe or listen to the testimony of a persecuted person before deportation.

11. Many refugee crises (Syria, Afghanistan, Myanmar) are linked to historical colonial or military interventions by democratic powers. Refoulement is a rejection of **Restorative Justice.

12.** The "Slippery Slope" of Rights- **Eg- devaluing the rights of its own marginalized citizens in future

13.** Failure of Communitarian Ethics **as nations are seen as part of a global "International Society" with mutual duties.

14.** C**auses **long-term psychological and ethical decay **in the host nation’s own moral fabric.

### Way Forward

1.** Individualized Screening- **Eg-l "Credible Fear" interview.

2.** Judicial Oversight **to ensure **Procedural Justice.

3.** Principle of Proportionality. **in Enforcement**

4.** Burden Sharing. Eg- EU Migration Pact

5. Enforcing **"Responsibility to Protect" **by UN

The ultimate best practice for a democratic society is to apply the **Rawlsian "Veil of Ignorance" **to every policy.

---

## Question 21 (Year: 2022 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2022-gs4-q21-civilsdaily**

**2022 - Russia and Ukraine war has been going on for the last seven months. Different countries have taken independent stands and actions keeping in view their own national interests. We are all aware that war has its own impact on the different aspects of society, including human tragedy. What are those ethical issues that are crucial to be considered while launching the war and its continuation so far? Illustrate with justification the ethical issues involved in the given state of affair.** [Year: 2022] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

"War does not determine who is right - only who is left." - **Bertrand Russell**

The Russia-Ukraine conflict serves as a grim case study for the tension between **Realpolitik **(national interest) and **Global Ethics.

**Stance by Different Countries**

| **Country** | **Stance** | **Primary National Interest** |

| --- | --- | --- |

| **USA & NATO** | **Military/Financial Aid** | **weakening Russia.** |

| **China** | **"Pro-Russia" Neutrality** | **weakening Western bloc dominance** |

| **India** | **Normative stance** | **Energy security (discounted oil)** |

| **EU Nations** | **Direct Support** | **Regional Security** |

### Impact of War on Different Aspects of Society

1.** Human Tragedy- **Russian casualties approaching **1.4 million **in 2025

2.** Displacement Crisis- **Over **14 million **Ukrainians

3.** Global Food Insecurity**

4.** Energy Volatility- **"energy poverty" for low-income households.

5.** Environmental "Ecocide"- **Eg- destruction of the Kakhovka Dam

6. "War Trauma" for an entire generation of children

7.** Erosion of **"Rules-Based Order" (violation of the UN Charter)

### Ethical issues to be considered while launching and continuing war

1. Adherence to principles of **Just War Theory **- **Jus ad Bellum **(the right to go to war) and **Jus in Bello **(right conduct within war).

**2. Impact on Human Rights**

    **a. Mass Casualties**

    **b. War inflation **disproportionately impacting poor

    **c. Refugee crisis**

3.** Violation of principle Proportionality. Eg- mass bombing of cities like Kiev

4.** Utilitarian principle **of ‘greatest happiness’ violated due to prolonged war.

5. Principle of **Last resort **not followed as Russian invasion was **preemptive.**

6.** Responsibility to future generations **violated. Eg- damage to infrastructure and ecology.

7.** Truth and transparency **principles not followed. Eg- online propaganda and misinformation.

8.** Global injustice **- Eg- Wheat shortages in Africa due to Black Sea blockade.

9.** Moral restraint in weapon use **not followed. Eg- cluster bomb and vaccum bomb used by Russia.

10. Reports of torture and summary executions of Prisoners of War violate the **Geneva Conventions**

**11. Failure in ensuring accountability for war crimes**

The war is a reflection of "rationality" becoming servant to "Will to Power." A just resolution requires **Jus post Bellum **framework (Justice after War)

---

## Question 22 (Year: 2023 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2023-gs4-q22-civilsdaily**

**2023 - ‘International aid’ is an accepted form of helping ‘resource-challenged’ nations.** [Year: 2023] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**Comment on ‘ethics in contemporary international aid’. Support your answer with suitable examples.**

"The proper aim of giving is to render the giver unnecessary." - **John Pulman**

In contemporary IR, the ethics of aid are often caught between **Cosmopolitanism **and **Realpolitik.

**Ethical principles of international aid**

1.** The Humanitarian Imperative- **Eg- aid to **Turkey and Syria after the 2023 earthquakes.

2.** Global Solidarity and Cosmopolitanism. Eg- India’s **vaccine maitri **initiative

3.** Distributive Justice- **Eg- **Norway's **commitment to spending 1% of its GNI on aid.

4.** Capacity Building **to realise **Right to development. **Eg- **India’s development assistance to Afghanistan **(Salma dam, parliament building)

5. Aid channeled through **global bodies **to ensure neutral distribution. Eg-**World Food Programme.

6.** Global Public Goods- **Eg- **COVAX **initiative for global vaccine equity during COVID-19.

7.** Peacebuilding **- Eg- Post-conflict reconstruction in Afghanistan.

8.** Climate justice **- Eg- Loss and damage fund for small island states.

9.** Gender justice **- Targeting women’s empowerment. Eg- Solar Mama’s of Africa

### Ethical Issues in Contemporary International Aid

1.** The Trap of "Tied Aid" (Economic Paternalism)- **Eg- **IMF structural adjustments **conditionalities

2.** Strategic Charity (Realpolitik)- **Aid is used as a bribe for UN votes or military access. Eg- **US aid to Pakistan.

3.** The "Debt Trap" Diplomacy **leading to a loss of sovereignty. Eg- **Hambantota Port in Sri Lanka**

4.** The "White Savior" Complex- **Designing solutions in Western boardrooms without local consultation.

5.** Corruption- **Eg- Diversion of humanitarian aid by **militias in Yemen **to fuel the ongoing conflict.

6.** Dependency Creation- **Constant aid stifle local industry and making a nation "addicted" to foreign help.

7.** Paternalistic Philanthropy- **Eg- Concerns over the **Gates Foundation’s **outsized influence on global malaria and polio policies.

8.** Lack of Transparency and accountability ("Black Box") **- Weak monitoring and evaluation.

9.** Neo-colonial influence **- Donors shaping domestic policies.

10.** Politicisation of aid **- Selective generosity based on alliances. Eg- prioritization of Ukrainian refugee by EU

11.** Short-termism **- Focus on visibility over sustainability.

For global “equity” and “justice” aid must be guided by principles of **transparency, localization, and long-term empowerment.**

---

## Question 23 (Year: 2024 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2024-gs4-q23-civilsdaily**

**2024 - “It is not enough to talk about peace, one must believe in it; and it is not enough to believe in it, one must act upon it.” In the present context, the major weapon industries of the developed nations are adversely influencing continuation of number of wars for their own self-interest, all around the world. What are the ethical considerations of the powerful nations in today’s international arena to stop continuation of ongoing conflicts?** [Year: 2024] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**“Wars begin where ethics ends.”**

In today’s world, conflicts persist not only because of political disputes but also due to powerful economic interests, especially the global arms industry.

### Role of major weapon industries in continuation of wars

1.** Profit motive **- Eg- Surge in global arms sales after Ukraine war.

2. Wars act as "testing grounds"

3.** Lobbying in **foreign policy. Eg- Military-industrial complex in the US.

4.** Arms exports to conflict zones **- Eg- Saudi Arabia as larget defence importer

5.** Proxy wars **- Eg- supply of arms to terrorist organisations

6.** Economic dependence **- Jobs and revenue from defence industry.

7. Capitalising on **security dilemma.**

### Ethical considerations for powerful nations to stop ongoing conflicts

1.** Deontology over Utilitarianism **by **prioritizing **duty to protect human life over GDP growth. Eg-Restrict arms to regimes violating human rights.

2.** Ethical assessment **of short and long term damage of war. Eg- over **1.4 million **Russian deaths in Ukraine war

3.** Responsibility to prevent harm **- Eg- Arms embargoes in active war zones.

4.** Non-complicity principle **to avoid moral responsibility for atrocities. Eg- Stopping arms to Saudi Arabia

during Yemen war.

5. Adherence to ethical standards of the **Arms Trade treaty**

| **Ethical Criterion** | **Description** |

| --- | --- |

| **Risk Assessment** | Probability of weapons fueling genocide |

| **Gender-Based Violence** | Probability of weapons facilitating sexual violence |

| **Diversion Control** | Risk of weapons ending in black market |

6.** Addressing Strategic Hypocrisy- **Eg- advocating for a "Rules-Based Order" while signing multi-billion dollar arms deals.

7.** Support for peace processes **- Eg- UN-led peace talks.

8.** Transparency and accountability **- Eg- Parliamentary approval for arms sales.

9.** Disarmament leadership. Eg- Nuclear disarmament treaties.

10.** Ethical foreign policy **- Values-based diplomacy over realpolitik.

11.** Corporate responsibility **- Eg- Arms export compliance laws.

12.** Transitioning to "Peace Economies". Eg- **Investing in **Green Technology **as alternatives to defense manufacturing

Real peace requires a **"Moral Disinvestment" **from war. This can be achieved by taming **"Will to Power" **of the defense industry by **"rationality" **and “**moral duty**” of the state.

---

## Question 24 (Year: 2025 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2025-gs4-q24-civilsdaily**

**2025 - Carl von Clausewitz once said, “War is a diplomacy by other means.” Critically analyse the above statement in the present context of contemporary geo-political conflict.** [Year: 2025] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

In his seminal work **On War, **Carl von Clausewitz **suggests that war is not an end in itself but a rational instrument of statecraft used to achieve political goals when traditional diplomatic dialogue fails.

### War is diplomacy by other means

1. Force used to extract **political concessions. Eg-Russia’s invasion of Ukraine to block NATO expansion.

2. War alters facts on ground to **strengthen bargaining position. Eg-Control of Crimea and Donbas.

3.** Power signalling **to deters rivals. Eg-China’s military exercises near Taiwan.

4. War reshapes **diplomatic alignments. Eg-Pakistan-China ‘all weather friendship’ after 1962 and 1965 wars

5.** Resource diplomacy **-Control over energy and minerals via force.

6.** Negotiation through attrition **-Prolonged fighting forces compromise. Eg-US withdrawl from Afghanistan

7.** Policy of ‘bait and bloodletting’. **Eg- US support to Ukraine to weaken Russia

8.** Peace enforcement. Eg-NATO intervention in Kosovo.

9. War is used as a tool for **regime change. **Eg- US intervention in Iraq

### Counter-argument- War is not diplomacy but its failure

1.** Humanitarian catastrophe **violates **utilitarian principle **of ‘greatest happiness’. Eg- over **1.4 million **Russian deaths in Ukraine war

2.** Rise of Non-State Actors- **Groups like **ISIS-K **dont pursue war for diplomatic aims but for ideological and religious aims.

3. War used to consolidate domestic **political legitimacy **rather than national interest. **Eg-Wartime

nationalism in Pakistan.

4. Due to ‘**complex interdependence’ **war as a diplomatic means is not a **rational choice. **Eg- US-China relations

5. War leads to **breakdown of diplomatic negotiations channels **for peaceful resolution. Eg- Security Council paralysis.

6. While diplomacy is based on reason war is based on **passion.

7. The acute **security dilemma and zero-sum mentality **fosters diplomatic distrust and reduce possibility of diplomatic cooperation. Eg- India’s suspension of Indus water treaty.

As per Deontological ethics, means of war cant justify any ends. As pointed out by **Bertrand Russell, **"War does not determine who is right - only who is left."

---

## Question 25 (Year: 2020 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2020-gs4-q25-civilsdaily**

**2020 - “Hatred is destructive of a person’s wisdom and conscience that can poison a nation’s spirit.’ Do you agree with this view? Justify your answer.** [Year: 2020] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

"Holding on to anger is like grasping a hot coal with the intent of throwing it at someone else; you are the one who gets burned." - **The Buddha**

**Hatred **is a deep-seated negative emotion marked by hostility, prejudice and desire to harm, which clouds moral judgement and rational thought.

### Hatred destroying a person’s wisdom and conscience

1.** Corruption of character (Virtue Ethics) **- prejudice and anger replace virtues like patience and tolerance. Eg- German society under Hitler

2.** Erosion of practical wisdom **and balanced judgement. Eg- Mob violence due to rumours on WhatsApp

3.** Loss of empathy **and compassion. Eg- In the **Rwandan Genocide (1994), Tutsis dehumanised as "cockroaches"

4.** Cognitive bias amplification **- Hatred confirms prejudice, not truth. Eg- Conspiracy theories about communities.

5. Stoics like **Marcus Aurelius **argued that hatred is a **"sickness of the soul." **Eg- torture of PoW or Concentration camps

6.** Vindictiveness over Justice- **A wise person seeks justice, while a hateful person seeks revenge. Eg-**Treaty of Versailles (1919) **was driven by French desire for "revenge"

7.** Violation of Kantian duty **- Treating others as means, not ends. Eg- "My Lai Massacre" during Vietnam war.

8.** Instrumentalisation of reason **- Intelligence used to harm, not to heal. Eg- doxxing

9.** Psychological degradation **- Hatred increases anxiety, anger, and stress. Eg- Radicalised individuals like Ajmal Kasab.

10.** Stagnation of Personal Growth- **Hateful person focuses on past grievances rather than on future or finding peace.

### Hatred Poisoning a Nation’s Spirit

1.** Erosion of Social Capital- **A nation’s spirit relies on "Fraternity." Hatred replaces cooperation with suspicion. Eg- communal riots during elections

2.** Institutional Decay- **When hatred enters the national spirit, institutions also get weaponized. Eg-

3.** The Normalization of Violence- **When hatred is mainstream, violence is seen as a "cleansing" act. Eg-ethnic cleansing of Jews in Nazi Germany

4.** Weakening of democratic culture. Eg- Labelling critics as anti-national.

5.** Fragmentation of national identity. Eg- Religion-based or ethnicity-based politics.

6.** The Post-Truth Nation- **propaganda takes over objective truth due to ‘superflous masses’.

7.** Global reputational damage. **Eg- **Apartheid regime in South Africa**

8.** The Cycle of Reciprocity- **Hatred in one group triggers hatred in another, creating a "Death Spiral." Eg- Ethnic conflict in Manipur

9.** Stifling of Creativity and Innovation **as hateful spirit is a closed spirit. Eg- **"Brain Drain" from 1930s Germany.

10.** Intergenerational Trauma- **Hatred is a legacy that ensures the spirit of the nation remains poisoned for decades. **Eg- Partition of India (1947)**

"Darkness cannot drive out darkness; only light can do that. Hate cannot drive out hate; only love can do that." - **Martin Luther King Jr.**

---

## Question 26 (Year: 2020 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2020-gs4-q26-civilsdaily**

**2020 - A positive attitude is considered to be an essential characteristic of a civil servant who is often required to function under extreme stress. What contributes to a positive attitude in a person?** [Year: 2020] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

"A man is but the product of his thoughts; what he thinks, he becomes." - **Mahatma Gandhi**

In public administration, a **positive attitude **is a mental and emotional mindset that focuses on constructive solutions, resilience, and optimism, even when faced with systemic constraints.

| **Extreme Stress** | **Role of Positive attitude** |

| --- | --- |

| **Crisis management** | **Objectivity **in decision making. Eg- T. N. Seshan |

| **Political pressure **- Eg- Transfer threats. | **Integrity and EI** |

| **Public scrutiny** | **Citizen centrality **to build public trust |

| **Law and order tensions **- Eg- Riots and protests | **Leading from the front for high team morale** |

| **Resource scarcity** | **Innovative problem solving. **Eg-crowdfunding |

| **Conflicting stakeholder interests. Eg-
Farmers vs industry land disputes. | **Empathy and calmness **to de-escalate tensions |

| **Moral dilemmas **- Eg- Truth vs Loyalty. | Ensuring **ethical consistency** |

| **Work-Life Imbalance** | **Endurance for **preventing "Burnout" |

**Developing a positive attitude is a process of "psychological conditioning" involving several factors-**

1.** Detachment (Nishkama Karma)- **Focus on the process, not just the result.

2.** Moral Clarity (Sense of Mission)- **Viewing work through the lens of a "higher calling." Eg-Commitment to public welfare.

3.** Emotional Intelligence (EQ)- **Recognizing and managing one’s own triggers through **‘mindfulness techniques’ **like **"Box Breathing" **(4-4-4-4 technique)

4.** Cognitive Reframing- **Viewing challenges as opportunities. Eg- Seeing a **punishment posting **as a chance to reform.

5.** Physical Well-being- **A healthy body serves as the "hardware" that supports the "software" of a positive mind.

6.** Social Support Systems (The "Ventilator" Effect)- **Eg- Spending quality time with **family or hobby groups **to decompress from official stress.

7.** Competence **and confidence is born from knowledge. Eg- domain specialisation among civil servants (Hota Committee)

8.** Gratitude and "Small Wins" - **Acknowledging incremental progress helps maintain morale when the "big picture" looks bleak.

9.** Intellectual Curiosity and Continuous Learning - **A mind that is constantly learning perceives "change" as exciting rather than threatening.

Thus, a positive attitude transforms a bureaucrat from a **"cog in the machine" into a leader of change.**

---

## Question 27 (Year: 2021 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2021-gs4-q27-civilsdaily**

**2021 - Attitude is an important component that goes as input in the delopement of human. How to build a suitable needed for a public servant?** [Year: 2021] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**Attitude **refers to a person’s predisposition to think, feel and act in a particular way. In the words of **Lou Holtz, "Ability is what you're capable of doing. Motivation determines what you do. Attitude determines how well you do it."**

### Importance of Attitude in the Development of Humans

1.** Knowledge Function- **Attitudes help humans **organize and simplify complex information. **Eg-positive attitude toward "Digital Governance" make it easier to implement new tech-tools.

2.** Ego-Defensive Function- **Protects self-esteem and emotional stability. Eg- Coping with failure without losing confidence.

3.** Value-Expressive Function- **Attitudes allow humans to express their central values.

4.** Instrumental function **- Guides behaviour to achieve rewards and avoid punishment.

5.** Adaptive (utilitarian) function **- Helps individuals adjust to social and professional environments

6. Attitude acts as a **"behavioral compass," **ensuring consistency in beliefs and actions, leading to a sense of "Wholeness."

7.** Decision-making function **- Influences judgement and choices.

### Ways to build a suitable attitude for a public servant

1. Internalising **constitutional and ethical values. **Eg- Ethics training at LBSNAA.

2.** Sensitivity Training **through **village immersion **programs for breaking the "Elite Bubble."

3. Practicing **Self-reflection **for recognising biases and emotional triggers. Eg- reflective journaling.

4. Developing **Emotional intelligence **through mindfulness and counselling sessions for managing stress and conflict constructively.

5.** Role modelling. Eg- **"Technocratic Optimism" **of E. Sreedharan for a solution-oriented attitude

6. Learning **responsibility **through transparency. Eg- Social audits and RTI processes.

7.** Continuous learning **for updating knowledge and perspectives. Eg- Mid-career training.

8.** Adversity Simulation - **Creating high-pressure scenarios in a controlled environment to build **resilience. **Eg- "crisis-room" simulation during training

9.** Peer-to-Peer De-biasing- **Group sessions to identify and dismantle hidden prejudices and develop **objectivity. **Eg- Using **Implicit Association Tests (IAT)**

10.** Feedback Loops- **Direct citizen interaction to develop compassion and leadership. Eg- Jan Sunwais
