11.** Historical Analysis of Failures **to build **Proactiveness. **Eg- Analyzing the **Bhopal Gas Tragedy **to foster an attitude of "Precautionary Vigilance" rather than "Post-facto Compliance."

These can help in shifting from a **"Command and Control" mindset **to **"Collaborate and Care" attitude **among public servants

---

## Question 28 (Year: 2022 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2022-gs4-q28-civilsdaily**

**2022 - The Rules and Regulations provided to all the civil servants are same, yet there is difference in the performance. Positive minded officers are able to interpret the Rules and Regulations in favour of the case and achieve success, whereas negative minded officers are unable to achieve goals by interpreting the same Rules and Regulations against the case. Discuss with illustrations.** [Year: 2022] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

In the realm of public administration, the rulebook provides the **"Letter of the Law," **but the officer's mindset provides the **"Spirit of the Law."**

**Alternative introduction**

Rules and regulations are meant to ensure **uniformity, legality and accountability **in

administration. However, their application depends on the **attitude, values and interpretation **of the officers.

### Positive-Minded Officers- Interpreting Rules for Success

1.** Invoking "Residual Powers" for Innovation. **Eg- IAS **Prashant Nair **used crowdfunding for community kitchens under **Project Compassion **in Kozhikode.

2.** Flexible during Emergencies. **Eg- procuring cylinders via "Spot Purchase" clause during COVID 19

3.** Promoting "Ease of Doing Business". **Eg- Interpreting licensing norms to encourage entrepreneurship.

4.** Utilizing "Spirit of the Law" **to uphold **justice **Eg- Allowing free treatment under government hospitals for undocumented homeless.

5. Adherence to **utilitarian **principle of **“greatest happiness” **by creative rule interpretation. **Eg- **using MNREGA funds to build school playgrounds

6.** Environmental Stewardship **using the "Precautionary Principle." Eg- Halting a project near a wetland by interpreting "Ecological Sensitivity" broadly

7.** Humanizing Service Rules- **Dealing with subordinates with empathy. **Eg- **Granting "Child Care Leave" to a single father

8.** Inclusive urban planning. Eg- Designating specific "Vending Zones" for street hawkers

9.** Active Conflict Resolution- Eg- **Using "Section 144" to create a "Protected Space" for a peaceful dialogue between administration and aggrieved public.

### Negative-Minded Officers- Interpreting Rules Against the Case

1. Suffers from **"Bureaucratic Apathy" **or **"Status Quo Bias." **Eg- resistance to "E-Office" by citing vague "Data Privacy" concerns.

2.** Red Tapism- **Eg- denying **ration **under PDS due to biometric error (Jharkhand case)

3.** "Passing the Buck"- **Interpreting jurisdiction rules to avoid taking responsibility. Eg- delay in medical aid in inter-state border accidents

4. Avoid **transparency and accountability. **Eg- invoking "National Security" clause to deny RTI

5.** Strict "Hierarchy" interpretation- Example- **Refusing to meet a citizen delegation because they did not have a "Prior Appointment".

6.** Focus on Punitive Action- **Interpreting discipline rules solely for punishment.

7.** Obstructive Auditing- **Using "Post-Facto" criticism to stall future initiatives.

8.** Resource Hoarding- **Refusing to spend funds to avoid "Audit Objections." Eg- consisting lapsing of **Tribe Sub-plan funds**

There is need to shift from a **"Command and Control" mindset **to **"Collaborate and Care" attitude **for transforming civil services from “rusted” steel frame to **“trusted steel frame”**

---

## Question 29 (Year: 2019 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2019-gs4-q29-civilsdaily**

**2019 - “Emotional Intelligence is the ability to make your emotions work for you instead of against you”. Do you agree with this view? Discuss.** [Year: 2019] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**Emotional Intelligence **is the capacity to recognise, understand, manage and use emotions constructively in oneself and in others.

“When awareness is brought to emotion, power is brought to your life.” - **Daniel Goleman**

**EI making emotions work for you**

**1. Self-awareness**

1.** Recognising emotions **before they control behaviour helps manage anger and frustration

2.** Understanding emotional triggers **helps in better preparation. Eg- Awareness of anxiety before public speaking.

3.** Realistic self-assessment **helps in knowing one’s strengths and weaknesses.

**2. Self-regulation**

    a. **Impulse control **- Prevents emotional

outbursts and rash decisions. Eg- Not shouting at subordinates during stress.

4.** Ensures emotional balance **- Eg- Calm leadership during disasters.

5.** Builds adaptability **to changing situations. Eg- Accepting e-governance by civil servants

**3. Motivation**

    a.** Positive drive **helps turn frustration into determination. Eg- Officers working overtime during elections to ensure fairness.

    b.** Optimism **despite setbacks. Eg- ISRO successfully launching Chandrayan 3 after failure of Chandrayan 2

**4. Empathy**

    a. Understanding others’ feelings and viewpoints helps developing **broader outlook and leadership**

    b.** Sensitivity to diversity **helps civil servants in handling community tensions sensitively.

**5. Social skills**

    a.** Effective communication **by expressing emotions constructively. Eg- PM addressing the nation during a pandemic.

    b.** Relationship building **- Eg- **Operation Sadbhavana **of Army in J&K for trust and cooperation with locals

### Counter-arguments- How Emotional Intelligence can make emotions work against you

**1. Emotional manipulation - **Eg- caste politics by leaders

**2. Emotion-reading skills can enable fake empathy and dishonesty.**

**3. Rationalising wrongdoing. **Eg- justifying corruption as “systemic necessity.”

**4. Emotional burnout **due to constant **emotional regulation**

5.** High empathy may lead **to compromise on objectivity and firmness

6.** Conflict avoidance **instead of **necessary confrontation.**

7.** Emotional intelligence without moral compass **becomes a tool of self interest

**Thus, EI + Integrity is needed to develop virtues of wisdom and compassion.**

---

## Question 30 (Year: 2020 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2020-gs4-q30-civilsdaily**

**2020 - What are the main components of emotional intelligence (EI)? Can they be learned? Discuss.** [Year: 2020] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**Emotional Intelligence **is the capacity to recognise, understand, manage and use emotions constructively in oneself and in others.

“When awareness is brought to emotion, power is brought to your life.” - **Daniel Goleman**

### Main Components of Emotional Intelligence

**1. Self-Awareness -**

    a. Involves recognizing your own emotions, strengths, weaknesses, and triggers in real-time.

    b.** Abraham Lincoln **recognised his "melancholy" and managed through humor, storytelling, and developing immense empathy

**2. Self-Regulation -**

    a. Involves managing and redirecting disruptive emotions and impulses.

    b. It prevents "Amygdala Hijack"-where the emotional brain takes over the rational brain.

    c. Eg- **Captain Sullenberger **- Regulated fear during engine failure to land safely on Hudson.

    d.** Warren Buffett’s emotional detachment **strategy - stay greedy when others are fearful

**3. Motivation-**

    a. Inner drive to pursue goals with energy and persistence

    b.** Eg- Marie Curie **worked in a shed for years to isolate radium.

    c.** Viktor Frankl **survived the Holocaust by finding "meaning" in his suffering. (Logotherapy)

**4. Empathy -**

    a. Ability to understand the emotions and perspectives of others.

    b. Essential for cross-cultural communication and building trust within a team.

    c. Eg- **Mahatma Gandhi- **lived like poor to "feel" their struggle.

**5. Social Skills -**

    a. Ability to manage relationships, build networks, resolve conflicts and inspire others.

    b.** Satish Dhawan (ISRO) **taking blame for SLV-3 mission failure

    c. Arif Sheikh leading “amcho police, amcho baster”

Unlike IQ, which is largely fixed by early adulthood, EI is based on **Neuroplasticity **- the brain's ability to form new neural pathways through repeated behavior. It can be learned through

### Self-Awareness

1.** Reflection and self-observation **through **mindfulness and meditation. Eg- Vipassana.

2.** Reflective journaling **- Writing daily emotional experiences and triggers.

3.** 360-degree feedback **from peers and seniors to reveal blind spots.

### Self-Regulation

1.** Stress-management training **to calm emotional arousal. Eg- "crisis-room" simulation in training

2.** Cognitive Reframing- **Viewing challenges as opportunities. Eg- Seeing a **punishment posting **as a chance to reform.

3.** Delay techniques **- Eg- 10-second rule before responding in anger.

4.** Physical regulation **- Exercise, sleep and breathing control helps in emotional stability.

### Motivation

1. Defining meaningful **personal and professional goals. **Eg- SMART goal frameworks.

2.** Positive psychology practices **-Eg- Writing three positive outcomes daily.

3.** Role Modelling. Eg- **"Technocratic Optimism" **of E. Sreedharan for a solution-oriented attitude

### Empathy

1.** Perspective-taking exercises **enhance empathy and understanding. Eg- **village immersion **programs

2.** Direct citizen interaction **exposes civil servants **to diversity **- develop compassion and leadership. Eg- Jan Sunwais

### Social Skills

1.** Communication skills training. Eg- Public speaking workshops.

2.** Life experiences **gradually deepen emotional understanding.

Thus, Emotional Intelligence is not innate or fixed. It is **learnable, trainable and improvable.**

---

## Question 31 (Year: 2021 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2021-gs4-q31-civilsdaily**

**2021 - In case of crisis of conscience does emotional intelligence help to overcome the same without compromising the ethical or moral stand that you are likely to follow? Critically examine.** [Year: 2021] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

A **crisis of conscience **arises when a person faces a conflict between personal values, professional duties, social pressures and moral principles. **EI **can play decisive role in navigating this crisis.

### Role of EI in overcoming crisis of conscience

**1. Self-awareness **helps identify moral discomfort early.

**2. Self-regulation **prevents panic, fear or anger from dictating action. ("Amygdala Hijack") Eg- **Sanjiv Chaturvedi (IFS) **exposing corruption in AIIMS

**3. EI **provides **Moral clarity **through reflection - prevents impulsive action.

**4. EI **builds **courage through emotional control **and enables ethical action. Eg- Whistleblowers like **Satyendra Dubey.**

**5.** EI developes **communication skills **that enables respectful dissent. Eg- **Mahatma Gandhi**

**6.** EI helps in **conflict management **without hostility. Eg- **Nelson Mandela **balancing justice and reconciliation.

**7.** It builds **resilience **to endure consequences of ethical action. Eg- punitive transfers of **Ashok Khemka**

**8. Empathy and perspective-taking **helps avoid moral absolutism and promotes fairness. Eg- Justice **V.R. Krishna Iyer **institutionalising PIL

**9. Inner peace **through EI reduces cognitive dissonance after ethical choice. Eg- **Satish Dhawan **taking responsibility for failure

**On the other hand, EI can also undermine ethical stand**

1. EI can be used to **justify **unethical actions. Eg- **bureaucrats **blaming “political pressure” to justify complicity.

2.** Rationalisation of wrongdoing **- Managing guilt instead of correcting behaviour. Eg- “sanskritization of corruption”

3.** Manipulation of others’ emotions. Eg- **Cult leaders like Jim Jones **emotionally controlled followers into mass suicide.

4.** Conflict avoidance **instead of **necessary confrontation. **Eg- **Corporate HR heads **ignoring harassment complaints to “avoid workplace disruption”.

5.** Institutional conformity **- EI helps individuals to adapt to unethical cultures. Eg- Eichmann committing atrocities under “orders” (banality of evil)

**6. Emotional burnout **due to constant **emotional regulation**

7.** High empathy may lead **to compromise on objectivity and firmness

8.** Ethical relativism **- Eg- Justifying censorship or surveillance as “necessary for public safety.”

Thus, EI is **value-neutral **and a **"means" to an "end." **It needs a strong **moral compass **to develop **virtuous character.**

---

## Question 32 (Year: 2023 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2023-gs4-q32-civilsdaily**

**2023 - What really matters for success, character, happiness and lifelong achievements is a definite set of emotional skills - your EQ- not just purely cognitive abilities that are measured by conventional IQ tests.” Do you agree with this view ? Give reasons in support of your answer.** [Year: 2023] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

In the modern world, **IQ **provides the technical "entry ticket" to a profession, but **EQ **determines how far an individual climbs and how meaningful their life becomes.

"In a high-IQ job pool, soft skills like discipline, drive, and empathy mark those who emerge as outstanding." -**Daniel Goleman**

### Importance of EQ

**For Professional Success**

- ** EQ **ensures **Leadership effectiveness. Eg- **Satya Nadella **transformed Microsoft by emphasising empathy and collaboration.

- Purely cognitive skills often freeze under extreme stress **("Amygdala Hijack"). **EQ provides calmness and resilience. Eg- **Captain "Sully" Sullenberger**

- EQ helps in building **effective Team Synergy **by providing "Psychological Safety" to members.

(Google’s **"Project Aristotle")

### For Character and Integrity

- EQ builds **Self-Regulation against Greed. **Eg- integrity of **Ashok Khemka**

- **•** It builds **moral courage **to endure consequences of ethical action. Eg- Whistleblowers like **Satyendra Dubey.**

- In high EQ person, **empathy **acts **as a Moral Compass. **Eg- **Mahatma Gandhi **lived like poor to "feel" their struggle.

### For Happiness and Well-being

- ** Self-awareness **allows individuals to recognize negative thought patterns before they lead to burnout.

- ** Inner peace **through EI reduces cognitive dissonance after ethical choice. Eg- **Satish Dhawan **taking responsibility for failure

- EQ helps build **healthy relationships and supportive social bonds. **Eg- open communication in family helping build trust

### For Lifelong Achievements

- ** Persistence **in the face of failure is an emotional skill, not an analytical one. **Eg- Thomas Edison **failed 1,000 times before inventing the lightbulb.

- ** Self-awareness **allows an individual to accept criticism and learn from mistakes.

- ** Adaptability- **In a changing world, the ability to "unlearn" and "relearn" requires emotional flexibility.

**Limitations of IQ**

1. Knowledge without integrity and EQ is **dangerous and dreadful. Eg- White-collar criminals**

2. High IQ does not ensure **emotional awareness. Eg- Brilliant engineers failing as managers due to poor people skills.

3.** Poor leadership capacity. **Eg- Sachin Teldulkar as a best batsman but poor captain

4. High vulnerability to **anxiety and stress. **Eg- rising suicide and depression among software engineers

5. High IQ does not ensure **interpersonal success. Eg- Isaac Newton had poor social relationships**

6. High IQ does not guarantee **adaptability. Eg- companies like Nokia, Kotak etc

To live a truly successful and happy life, one must balance the **logic of the head **with the **intelligence of the heart.**

---

## Question 33 (Year: 2021 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2021-gs4-q33-civilsdaily**

**2021 - Identify five ethical traits on which one can plot the performance of a civil servant. Justify their inclusion in the matrix.** [Year: 2021] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

"The civil service is not a service of status, but a service of responsibility. It is a commitment to the conscience of the nation." - **Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel**

The performance of a civil servant cannot be measured merely by **targets achieved, **but must be evaluated through the **lens of ethical conduct.**

**1. Integrity (Consistency and Honesty) - **It implies that the officer's actions are consistently aligned with their stated moral values, regardless of external pressure.

- **Justification**

o Builds **public trust **on reliability and honesty of administration.

o **G**ives **moral courage **to say "No" to illegal orders from political superiors.

o Ensures **consistency, **predictably and adherence to the code of conduct.

o **Eg- Ashok Khemka (IAS)**

**2. Objectivity (Rationality and Merit) - **ensures that decisions are based on evidence, logic, and the rule of law, rather than personal bias, nepotism, or political leanings.

- **Justification**

o **Fairness- **It ensures equal treatment of every citizen

o **Promotes meritocracy **and **efficiency**

o Decisions are less likely to be overturned by courts.

o **Eg- E. Sreedharan **- objectivity in the awarding of contracts for the Delhi Metro.

**3. Compassion and Empathy (Human-Centric Service) - **involves understanding the pain of the citizens and acting to alleviate it.

- ** Justification-**

o **E**nsures that the "spirit of the law" is used to achieve **Social Justice**

o Brings **democratic ethos **into civil services (instead of rigidity and indifference)

o Helps understand **ground realities.**

**o Improves welfare delivery effectiveness.**

- ** Eg- Armstrong Pame (IAS)**- build a 100km road via crowdfunding

**4. Accountability (Responsibility and Transparency) - It **is the obligation of an official to be answerable for their decisions and the consequences thereof.

- ** Justification-**

o **P**revents the arbitrary use of discretionary powers.

o **Improves transparency and legitimacy.**

o **Encourages better performance standards.**

o **Builds democratic credibility.**

- ** Eg- Vinod Rai **exposed "presumptive losses" in the 2G Spectrum and Coal block allocations.

**5. Emotional Intelligence**

- **• Justification**

o Enables calm decision-making under pressure.

o Improves conflict resolution and negotiation.

o Builds trust and team cohesion.

o Enhances ethical judgement by integrating empathy and reason.

o Eg- **Krishna Teja (IAS) **coordinated evacuation during Kerala floods

These values ensure that governance is not only efficient but **ethical, humane and resilient.**

---

## Question 34 (Year: 2021 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2021-gs4-q34-civilsdaily**

**2021 - Identify ten essential values that are needed to be an effective public servant. Describe the ways and means to prevent non-ethical behaviour in the public servants.** [Year: 2021] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

Effective public service is built on the foundation of the **"Spirit of Service" **and **"Constitutional Morality."**

### Ten Essential Values for an Effective Public Servant

1.** Integrity- **“Integrity is doing the right thing even when no one is watching.” Eg- **Ashok Khemka**

2.** Objectivity- **Making decisions based on merit, data, and logic rather than personal bias, nepotism, or political pressure.

3.** Neutrality- **Providing the same quality of service and advice regardless of which political party is in power. Eg- **T.N. Seshan**

4.** Empathy and Compassion- **Sensing the pain of the citizens and using the law to alleviate their suffering. Eg- **S. Shankaran **in implementing **Bonded Labour Abolition Act**

5.** Accountability- **Taking full ownership of decisions and outcomes.

6.** Transparency **and **openness **in decision making. Eg- proactive disclosure under RTI

7.** Dedication to Public Service- **Eg- **Armstrong Pame (IAS) **built a 100km "People's Road" in Manipur through crowdfunding.

8.** Fortitude (Moral Courage)- **Eg- Whistleblowers like **Satyendra Dubey.**

9.** Probity- **Strict adherence to ethical standards in public life, especially in financial and decision matters

10.** Efficiency and Economy- **following **utilitarian maxim **of ‘greatest happiness’ Eg- **E. Sreedharan **finishing mega-projects ahead of schedule and under budget.

### Ways and Means to Prevent Non-Ethical Behavior

### Internal Controls

- "Value-based Training" during induction and mid-career. (2nd ARC)

- ** Emotional Intelligence (EI)- **Teaching officers to manage stress and "Amygdala Hijack"

- Transitioning from a rigid "Code of Conduct" (punitive) to a **"Code of Ethics" **(aspirational).

### External Controls

- Strengthening bodies like the **Lokpal, Lokayukta, and CVC **to investigate complaints without political interference.

- ** E-Governance- **Reducing human interface in public service delivery to eliminate the "discretionary space." Eg- DBT

- ** Independent Office of Ethics **to oversee financial disclosures and provide ethics counseling to officers.

(US model)

- Institutionalising **Integrity Pacts **(OECD/Transparency International recommendation)

### Empowering the Citizen (Social Controls)

- ** Social Audits- **Eg- MGNREGA social audits in Andhra Pradesh

- ** Strengthening RTI. **Eg- mandatory disclosures under section 4

- ** Institutionalising Citizen's Charters **based on **Sevottam Model**

“Power tends to corrupt, and absolute power corrupts absolutely, unless restrained by ethics and accountability.”

---

## Question 35 (Year: 2021 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2021-gs4-q35-civilsdaily**

**2021 - Should impartial and being non-partisan be considered as indispensable qualities to make a successful civil servant? Discuss with illustrations.** [Year: 2021] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

A civil servant derives legitimacy not from popular mandate but from the **trust of neutrality, fairness and rule-based conduct.

**Impartiality **is the quality of making decisions based on objective criteria, merit, and facts.

**Non-partisanship **is a state of being politically neutral and serving the government with equal dedication, regardless of personal political leanings.

### Importance of Impartiality

1. Impartiality ensures that **all citizens are treated equally **regardless of status, identity or political affiliation. Eg- Kiran Bedi towing vehicle of PM

2. Maintaining **Public Trust and belief in fairness **of administration - strengthens legitimacy. Eg- UPSC selection process

3.** Promotes inclusivity and Social Justice- **Eg- **S. Shankaran **in implementing the **Bonded Labour Abolition Act**

4.** Prevents misuse of power. Eg- **Ashok Khemka (IAS) **cancelled illegal land deals irrespective of political interests.

5.** Enables fair grievance redressal. Eg- **U Sagayam (IAS) **conducted impartial inquiries into granite mining.

6. Ensures **efficiency in resource utilization. Eg- **E. Sreedharan **ensuring objectivity in the awarding of contracts for the Delhi Metro.

7. Promotes **professional ethics **by ensuring adherence to principles of neutrality, selflessness and accountability.

### Importance of Non-partisanship

1.** Continuity of Government- **Eg- The smooth transition of power in India since independence

2.** Fearless Advice **on the legality of a political directive.

3.** Efficient Crisis Management- **In communal or ethnic tensions, an impartial officer is the only trusted mediator.

4. It prevents the **"cooking of books" **(like GDP or employment figures) to suit a political party's re-election campaign.

5.** Prevents politicisation of bureaucracy. **Eg- **Durga Shakti Nagpal **resisting political interference.

6.** Maintains professional autonomy. **Eg- RBI independence in monetary policy.

7. Prevents **authoritarian tendencies and ‘spoils system.’**

8. Safeguards **rule of law **by resisting politically motivated actions. Eg- EC’s fair application of MCC

Thus, impartiality and non-partisanship are **cardinal virtues for **preserving **democratic fairness **as well as **institutional and ethical integrity.**

---

## Question 36 (Year: 2022 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2022-gs4-q36-civilsdaily**

**2022 - Apart from intellectual competency and moral qualities, empathy and compassion are some of the other vital attributes that facilitate the civil servants to be more competent in tackling the crucial issues or taking critical decisions. Explain with suitable illustrations.** [Year: 2022] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**“The purpose of power is to serve, not to rule.” **To adhere to this ethos, civil servants needs combination of IQ, ethics and compassion.

### Intellectual Competency

1.** Analytical Ability- **Eg- **V.K. Pandian (IAS) **used data analytics in sports governance in Odisha.

2.** Technological Literacy- **Eg- **J. Satyanarayana (IAS) **pioneered the 'e-Seva' project

3.** Domain Expertise- **Eg- **Dr. M. S. Swaminathan **(Green Revolution)

4.** Professionalism. **Eg- Sreedhran

5.** Legal Acumen. **Eg- **S.R. Sankaran (IAS) **used land laws to restore land to marginalized tribals.

6.** Communication Skills**

7.** Innovation- **Eg- IAS **Prashant Nair **used crowdfunding for community kitchens

### Moral Qualities

1.** Integrity- **Eg- **C.G. Somiah (IAS)**- unblemished career as the CAG of India.

2.** Fortitude- **Eg- **U. Sagayam (IAS), spent a night in a graveyard to protect evidence in a mining scam.

3.** Probity- **Eg- **Satyendra Dubey (IES) **exposed corruption in the Golden Quadrilateral project.

4.** Accountability **and **transparency. **Eg- **Satish Dhawan **taking blame for SLV-3 mission failure

5.** Impartiality- **Eg- **T.N. Seshan as CEC**

6.** Selflessness- **Eg- **Randhir Prasad Verma **(IPS) sacrificed his life while fighting armed robbers

### Importance of Empathy and Compassion

1. Empathy helps in prioritizing **utilitarian virtue of “greatest good” **over self-interest.

2.** Humanizing the Rule of Law- **Ensures rules don't become tools of oppression. **Eg- **authorizing PDS ration for a poor with leprosy.

3.** Bridging the Trust Deficit- **Compassion builds a bond between the state and the citizen.

4.** Conflict De-escalation (building social capital)- Eg- P. Vijayakumar (IPS) **using empathetic negotiation to prevent communal flares in Coimbatore.

5.** Inclusive Infrastructure- **Eg- **Dr Nidhi Patel **pioneering space lab for rural students in Bilaspur.

6.** Rehabilitation over Punishment- Eg- Kiran Bedi **introduced Vipassana and education in Tihar.

7.** Resource Mobilization- **A compassionate officer inspires others to give. **Eg- Armstrong Pame (IAS) **built a 100km "People’s Road" using crowdfunding

8.** Going beyond administrative duty **to help others. **Eg- Inayat Khan (IAS) **adopted the daughters of CRPF martyrs

9. Compassion guides in using **discretionary powers **in an ethical manner. Eg- delaying the demolition of encroachment until finalization of the rehabilitation **plan.**

10.** Vulnerability Mapping- **Empathy helps civil servants to identify those who don't have a "voice." Eg-Tamboli Ayyaj building hospitals for Adivasi’s in maoist areas.

Thus, empathy and compassion enable civil servants to convert **authority into service and law into justice.**

## Question 37 (Year: 2021 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2021-gs4-q37-civilsdaily**

**2021 - Besides domain knowledge, a public official needs innovativeness and creativity of a high order as well, while resolving ethical dilemmas. Discuss with suitable examples.** [Year: 2021] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

“In times of complexity, imagination is more important than knowledge.” - **Albert Einstein**

Innovativeness and creativity enable officials to find **morally acceptable and practically workable **solutions.

### Ethical Dilemmas in Civil Services

1.** Development vs. Displacement- **Narmada Bachao Andolan (Medha Patkar vs. State).

2.** Confidentiality vs. Transparency- **Whistleblowing

3.** Political Pressure vs. Neutrality**

4.** Freedom of Speech vs. Public Order**

5.** Environment vs. Livelihood**

6.** Efficiency vs. Equity**

7.** Personal Ethics vs. Professional Duty**

8.** Loyalty vs. Truth**

### Importance of Domain Knowledge

1.** Policy Formulation- Dr. Manmohan Singh’s **economic expertise during the 1991 reforms.

2.** Infrastructure Excellence- E. Sreedharan’s **engineering mastery in the Delhi Metro.

3.** Economic Management- Raghuram Rajan’s **knowledge of monetary policy at the RBI.

4.** Scientific Progress- Dr. A.P.J. Abdul Kalam’s **aerospace knowledge in the Missile Program.

5.** Legal Accuracy- T.N. Seshan’s **deep understanding of Constitutional Law as CEC.

6.** Health Administration- Dr. Gagandeep Kang’s **virology expertise during vaccine development.

7.** Agricultural Transformation- Dr. M.S. Swaminathan **in the Green Revolution.

8.** Digital Governance- Nandan Nilekani’s **tech background in the creation of Aadhaar.

9.** Financial expertise- Vinod Rai’s **auditing expertise as the CAG of India.

### Need for Innovation and Creativity to Resolve Ethical Dilemmas

1.** Resource optimization- **Eg- **Armstrong Pame (IAS) **crowdfunded the "People’s Road".

2.** Reformative justice- Kiran Bedi (IPS) **introduced Vipassana in Tihar to reform rather than just punish.

3. Prioritising **social welfare **by bypassing bureaucratic rigidity. Eg- **Prashant Nair’s **"Operation Sulaimani" - Use of crowdsourced coupons to feed hunger

4. Innovative solutions for **winning ‘hearts and minds’ **and delegitimizing insurgency. Eg- **Saurabh Kumar (IAS) **built "Education City" in Dantewada.

5. Finding **‘out of the box’ solutions. Eg- IPS **chetan singh Rathore **using National Anthem to manage protesting crowd.

6. Helps in **effective management of crisis situations. Eg- **Dr. Syed Sehrish Asgar **used her office as a "human call center" during communication blackouts in J&K

7. Helps in **collaborative problem solving **rather than a top-down approach. Eg- S.R. Sankaran **involved local community elders in identifying bonded laborers.

8. Creativity and innovations facilitate adoption of technology to solve problems. Eg- **Dr. Hari Chandana **building pavements from recycled plastic in Hyderabad.

9. Can help address **social stigma **associated with manual work. **Eg- Ritu Sain (IAS) **turned waste-pickers into "Green Commandos".

Ethical governance today requires not just knowledge of rules but **moral imagination, contextual intelligence and creative problem-solving.

### Answer

**“The purpose of power is to serve, not to rule.” **To adhere to this ethos, civil servants must imbibe certain universal values of **‘Ethical Governance.’**

**Three basic values and their importance**

**Integrity (Honesty and probity in conduct) - **Acting truthfully, transparently and consistently with moral and legal standards.

- **• Importance-**

- Prevents corruption and misuse of public office.

- Builds citizens’ trust in institutions.

- Protects fairness in decision-making.

- Strengthens legitimacy of the state.

- **• Illustration- **Sanjiv Chaturvedi (IFS) exposed corruption in AIIMS despite facing harassment. **Impartiality (Fairness and non-discrimination) - **Treating all individuals and groups equally, without bias based on identity, status or political affiliation.

- ** Importance-**

3.

• Upholds equality before law.

- Prevents favouritism and discrimination.

- Stability during Political Transitions

- Impartial officer acts as a trusted mediator in conflict resolution

- ** Illustration- **T.N. Seshan, as CEC, enforcing MCC in fair manner.

**Accountability - **Being answerable for decisions and taking responsibility for consequences.

- **• Importance-**

• **Feedback Loop-**facilitates a two-way communication between

state and citizens

- Improves transparency and performance.

- Enables democratic control over bureaucracy.

- Promotes ethical and careful decision-making.

- **• Illustration - **Ashwini Vaishnaw took moral responsibility after the Odisha train accident by personally overseeing relief and restoration.

### Other values (Nolan Principles)

**1. Selflessness**

**2. Objectivity**

**3. Openness**

**4. Leadership**

**5. Commitment to constitutional morality**

**6. Probity**

**7. Empathy and Compassion**

**8. Anonymity**

These values ensure that **"Steel Frame" **does not **rust or bend **under the weight of corruption and bias.

### Answer

Public life refers to the **activities and roles **individuals undertake in the service of the community, whether as elected representatives, civil servants, or members of public bodies.

**Nolan Principles**

1.** Selflessness**

2.** Integrity**

3.** Objectivity**

**4. Openness**

**5. Leadership**

6.** Accountability**

7.** Honesty**

8.** Leadership**

**Indian constitutional ethos**

**1. Transparency**

**2. Impartiality**

**3. Responsiveness**

**4. Commitment to public interest**

1.** Integrity (Honesty and probity in conduct) - **Acting truthfully, transparently and consistently with moral and legal standards.

- **• Importance-**

- Prevents corruption and misuse of public office.

- Builds citizens’ trust in institutions.

- Protects fairness in decision-making.

- Strengthens legitimacy of the state.

- **• Illustration- **Sanjiv Chaturvedi (IFS) exposed corruption in AIIMS despite facing harassment.

2. **Impartiality (Fairness and non-discrimination) - **Treating all individuals and groups equally, without bias based on identity, status or political affiliation.

- **Importance-**

- Upholds equality before law.

- Prevents favouritism and discrimination.

- Stability during Political Transitions

- Impartial officer acts as a trusted mediator in conflict resolution

- **Illustration- **T.N. Seshan, as CEC, enforcing MCC in fair manner.

3. **Accountability - **Being answerable for decisions and taking responsibility for consequences.

- **• Importance-**

- ** Feedback Loop- **facilitates a two-way communication between state and citizens

- Improves transparency and performance.

- Enables democratic control over bureaucracy.

- Promotes ethical and careful decision-making.

- **• Illustration - **Ashwini Vaishnaw took moral responsibility after the Odisha train accident by personally overseeing relief and restoration.

These values ensure that **"Steel Frame" **does not **rust or bend **under the weight of corruption and bias.

## Question 40 (Year: 2022 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2022-gs4-q40-civilsdaily**

**2022 - Write short notes on the following in 30 words each -** [Year: 2022] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

1.** Constitutional Morality - **Adherence to the core philosophies of the Constitution even when they clash with popular social norms or traditional beliefs.

**Key pillars**

    a.** Rule of Law **- Eg- Article 14

    b.** Institutional Integrity **- Eg- autonomy of EC, CAG

    c.** Progressive Interpretation **- Eg- right to privacy

    d.** Equality and Dignity **- Eg- Sabrimala Judgment

    e.** Constitutional Values **- Upholding justice, liberty, equality, fraternity

    f.** Separation of Powers **and **Checks and Balances**

2.** Conflict of Interest - **A situation where a public official’s private interests could improperly influence their official decisions. Eg- **Chanda Kochar case**

### Reasons

    a. Dual roles - official and private interests overlapping

    b. Post-retirement employment expectations (revolving door)

    c. Political affiliations or ideological bias

    d. Gifts, hospitality and favours from stakeholders

    e. Weak disclosure and transparency mechanisms

    f. Discretionary power

    g. Lack of ethical awareness and training

3.** Probity in Public Life - **The quality of having strong moral principles, including absolute honesty, transparency, and the active application of integrity in every administrative action. **Eg- U. Sagayam (IAS) **- 1st IAS office to declare his personal assets

Key pillars

    a. Integrity and Honesty

    b. Transparency and accountability

    c. Impartiality and objectivity

    d. Ethical leadership

4.** Challenges of Digitalization**

    **a. Digital Divide (Rural-Urban & Gender Gap)**

    **b. Cybersecurity and Financial Fraud. **Eg- digital arrests

    **c. Inclusion - Exclusion errors. **Eg- Jharkhand PDS case

    **d. Data Privacy and Surveillance Concerns**

    **e. Digital Illiteracy**

5.** Devotion to Duty - **The unwavering commitment to professional obligations, often involving extreme personal sacrifice and prioritizing public welfare over personal comfort.

Examples

    a.** Randhir Prasad Verma **(IPS) sacrificed his life while fighting armed robbers

    b. Whistleblowers like **Satyendra Dubey**

    c.** S.R. Sankaran - “an ideal people's IAS officer” **remained unmarried for service of nation

## Question 41 (Year: 2018 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2018-gs4-q41-civilsdaily**

**2018 - What is meant by public interest? What are the principles and procedures to be followed by the civil servants in public interest?** [Year: 2018] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

Public interest is a broad, dynamic concept **that refers to the **welfare, well-being, and general good **of the community as a whole and prioritizing **collective benefits **over individual or sectional advantages.

"A public official is a fiduciary of the public’s interest." - **Paul H. Douglas**

### Principles to be Followed in Public Interest

1.** Maxim of utilitarianism - **“greatest happiness of greatest number”

2.** Selflessness- **Prioritizing public gain over personal material benefits.

3.** Integrity- **Absolute consistency between one's values and actions.

4.** Objectivity- **Making decisions based solely on merit, facts, and evidence. Eg- E. Sreedharan in awarding delhi metro projects

5.** Accountability- **Being answerable for the consequences of administrative decisions. Eg- **Lal Bahadur Shastri **resigning as Railway Minister following a major train accident.

6.** Openness (Transparency)- **Proactively sharing information to foster public trust. Eg- **U. Sagayam (IAS) **- 1st IAS office to declare his personal assets

7.** Impartiality- **Acting without bias toward any caste, creed, or political affiliation. Eg- T. N. Seshan as CEC

8.** Empathy and Compassion- **Sensitivity toward the plight of the marginalized. Eg- **Prashant Nair’s **"Operation Sulaimani" - Use of crowdsourced coupons to feed hunger

9.** Commitment to Public Service- **Viewing the job as a “mission”. Eg- **Dr. Rajendra Bharud (IAS) **setting up an oxygen plant in tribal Nandurbar before the second COVID wave

10.** Leadership- **Leading by example to uphold ethical standards. Eg- **S.R. Sankaran - “an ideal people's IAS officer” **remained unmarried for service of nation

11.** Courage of Conviction- **Eg- **Durga Shakti Nagpal (IAS) **taking a firm stand against the powerful sand mining mafia in Noida.

### Procedures to be Followed in Public Interest

1. Adherence to **code of conduct **and **code of ethics**

2.** Adherence to the Rule of Law- **Every decision must be rooted in constitutional or statutory authority

3.** Due Process in Procurement- **Eg- using **GeM-Government e-Marketplace.

4.** Public Consultation- **Eg- "Gram Sabhas" or "Jan Sunwais" before major projects

5.** Grievance Redressal Mechanisms- **Eg- **CPGRAMS**

6.** Recusal from Conflict of Interest**

7.** Evidence-Based Policy Making- **Eg- GATI Shakti mission

These principles and procedures ensure that governance is not only efficient but **ethical, humane and resilient.**

---

## Question 42 (Year: 2018 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2018-gs4-q42-civilsdaily**

**2018 - Explain the process of resolving ethical dilemmas in Public Administration.** [Year: 2018] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

An **ethical dilemma **in public administration occurs when a public official is faced with a choice between two or more competing values or interests.

**^^hi'cJ choice ---) Trtner Pe^co-**

i|N«d1<pn^ , Di)4K)H)q^ ^Qr^hicaJ Choice—5 C^>5 of COhSn'jthrP

### Ethical Dilemmas in Civil Services

1.** Development vs. Displacement- **Narmada Bachao Andolan (Medha Patkar vs. State).

2.** Confidentiality vs. Transparency- **Whistleblowing

3.** Political Pressure vs. Neutrality**

4.** Freedom of Speech vs. Public Order**

5.** Environment vs. Livelihood**

6.** Efficiency vs. Equity**

7.** Personal Ethics vs. Professional Duty**

8.** Loyalty vs. Truth**

### Process of Resolving Ethical Dilemmas

**1. Identification of the Ethical Issue - **clearly define the conflicting values and recognize the stakes for all parties involved is the primary step.

**2. Information Gathering - **collect all relevant data, consult subject matter experts, and understand the ground reality of the situation.

**3. Analyzing the Legal Framework - **The decision must first pass the test of **Legality.

**4. Applying Ethical Frameworks for evaluating options**

- ** Utilitarianism- **Which choice brings the "greatest good for the greatest number"? • **Deontology- **What is my absolute "Duty" as a public servant?

- ** Social Justice (Rawls)- **Does this decision benefit the "least advantaged" member of society?

- The “**middle path**” to balance the extremes.

5.** Assess the impact **of various options on different stakeholders.

6.** Final Decision and Review - **After choosing the most ethical path, the official should implement the decision and monitor its impact for course correction.

Resolving ethical dilemmas is an exercise in **Constitutional Morality. Under **Mahatma Gandhi’s Talisman, the ultimate resolution of any dilemma lies in whether the decision empowers the weakest.

---

## Question 43 (Year: 2019 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2019-gs4-q43-civilsdaily**

**2019 - What do you understand by the term ‘public servant’? Reflect on the expected role of public servant.** [Year: 2019] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

A **public servant **is an individual entrusted by the state to exercise authority and perform functions on behalf of society in order to implement laws, deliver public services and protect citizens’ rights and welfare.

"A public official is a fiduciary of the public’s interest." - **Paul H. Douglas**

### The Expected Role of a Public Servant

7.** Upholder of Integrity- **Resisting bribes and external

pressures to maintain professional standards. Eg- **U. Sagayam (IAS) **declaring his assets publicly.

8.** Leader by Example- **Inspiring subordinates to work with the same level of dedication and ethics. Eg-**Kiran Bedi (IPS) **reforming Tihar jail

9.** Impartial Arbitrator- **Resolving disputes between different social or economic groups without bias. Eg-**R.N. Ravi, **played a pivotal role in the Naga peace talks

10.** Empathetic Listener- **Being accessible to the grievances of the poorest citizens.

11.** Innovator in Governance- **Finding low-cost, high-impact solutions to local problems. Eg- IAS **Prashant Nair **used crowdfunding for community kitchens

12.** Protector of the Marginalized- **Ensuring that the **"last person" (Antyodaya) **receives the benefits of the state. Eg- **Dr Nidhi Patel **pioneering space lab for rural students in Bilaspur.

13.** Crisis Manager- **Providing leadership during natural disasters or civil unrest. Eg- **Dr. Rajendra Bharud (IAS) **setting up an oxygen plant in tribal Nandurbar before the second COVID wave

14.** Regulatory Watchdog- **Ensuring that private entities follow safety and ethical standards. Eg- **Vinod Rai **as CAG exposed "presumptive losses" in the 2G Spectrum and Coal block allocations.

15.** Environmental Steward- **Eg- **Dr. Hari Chandana **building pavements from recycled plastic in Hyderabad.

"The civil service is not a service of status, but a service of responsibility. It is a commitment to the conscience of the nation." - **Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel**

---

## Question 44 (Year: 2019 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2019-gs4-q44-civilsdaily**

**2019 - “Non-performance of duty by a public servant is a form of corruption”. Do you agree with this view? Justify your answer.** [Year: 2019] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

“The greatest corruption is the corruption of duty.” - **Edmund Burke**

Conventionally, corruption is viewed as the "misuse of public office for private gain," however, in a broader ethical sense, **omission **(failing to act) is as damaging as **commission **(acting wrongly).

**Non-performance of duty as form of corruption 1. Breach of the "Social Contract" - **The public pays taxes in exchange for services. Non-performance is a unilateral breach of this trust.

projects

6. Inaction is a betrayal of the **"fiduciary duty" **owed to the citizens. Eg- Police officers failing to register an FIR in SC, ST atrocity cases.

7.** Wastage of Resources- **Eg- food grains roting in **FCI **godowns while tribal populations suffer from malnutrition.

8. When officials don't work, citizens **lose faith in democracy **and turn to **extra-constitutional means for justice. **Eg- **rise of "vigilante justice"**

9.** Moral hazard - **Inaction normalises irresponsibility.

10.** Facilitates exploitation. Eg- Labour inspectors not enforcing minimum wage laws.

### Ways to Curb Corruption and Non-Performance

1.** Code of Ethics & Code of Conduct. (2nd ARC)**

2.** Implementation of Citizens’ Charters- **Eg- SAKALA (Karnataka Guarantee of Services Act)

3. Giving legal backing to **Social Audits**

4.** Leveraging Technology. **Eg- Faceless Income Tax Assessment

5. Strengthening the **Lokpal and Lokayuktas **to investigate "maladministration" and "neglect"

6.** Independent Commission Against Corruption - "Hong Kong Model"**

**7. Performance-linked accountability. **Eg- 360 degree feedback

A culture of **active responsibility, diligence and accountability **is needed to deal with the menace of corruption.
