## Question 45 (Year: 2025 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2025-gs4-q45-civilsdaily**

**2025 - “One who is devoted to one’s duty attains highest perfection in life.” Analyse this statement with reference to a sense of responsibility and personal fulfilment as a civil servant.** [Year: 2025] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

“Your right is to work only, but never to its fruits.” - **Bhagavad Gita**

The statement reflects the idea of **Karma-Yoga **- that sincere devotion to one’s duty leads to both moral excellence and inner fulfilment. For a civil servant, devotion to duty converts power into service.

### Devotion to Duty leading to Sense of Responsibility

1. For a civil servant, duty is not just a job description, it is a **moral contract **with the sovereign the people. **(Trusteeship principle)**

2. Devotion ensures that the officer is **upholding Constitutional Morality **even under political pressure.

3.** Professional Integrity- **It manifests as doing the right thing when no one is watching. Eg- **Satyendra Dubey**

4.** Accountability to the "Last Person"- **A devoted officer views themselves as answerable to the most marginalized. Eg- **Dr. Rajendra Bharud **(IAS) - oxygen plants in tribal Nandurbar district.

5.** Impartiality in Crisis- **Devotion **prevents personal biases **from clouding administrative judgment.

6.** Resource Stewardship- **Eg- **E. Sreedharan **completed Metro projects under budget and ahead of time.

7.** Compassionate Regulation- **Balancing the "letter of the law" with the "spirit of justice." Eg- delaying the demolition of encroachment until finalization of the rehabilitation **plan.**

8.** Crisis Leadership- **Eg- **Krishna Teja (IAS) **coordinated evacuation of over 2.5 lakh people during Kerala floods

9. Acts as a Internal moral compass ensuring **accountability to conscience. Eg - Satish Dhawan taking responsibility for ISRO failure.

### Devotion to Duty leading to Personal Fulfilment

1. Personal fulfilment in civil service comes from the **alignment of one's "inner conscience" with "outer action."**

1.** Self-Actualization- **Finding the highest version of oneself through service.

2.** Emotional Intelligence- **Developing a sense of **"Wholeness" **by connecting with the suffering and joy of the public.

3.** The "Flow" State- **Becoming so absorbed in problem-solving that work stops being stressful and becomes meditative.

4.** Legacy Building- S.R. Sankaran - “an ideal people's IAS officer” **remained unmarried for service of nation

5.** Inner Peace- **knowing there is no gap between what you believe and what you do.

6.** Building Social Capital and Respect. **Eg- **Prashant Nair **(IAS) being called "Collector Bro" by the youth of Kozhikode

7.** Resilience- **Devotion provides the "buffer" against the frustrations of transfers or political interference.

8.** A Clear Conscience- **The ability to sleep peacefully, knowing one has not been a party to injustice

9.** Transcendence- **Moving beyond the "ego" (the I, Me, Mine) to a larger identity (The State, The People).

10.** Institution building **by prioritizing long-term public interest over short-term gain. Eg- **Verghese Kurien building AMUL.**

### Devotion to Duty leading to Highest Perfection

1. "Highest Perfection" is the state where the administrator becomes an **"Ethical Titan"**

2. Sense of responsibility and fulfillment leads to **unity of**

**thought, word, and deed - **a state of perfection. Eg- Mahatma Gandhi

3.** Achieves Equanimity (Samatvam)- **Remaining calm in both praise and blame, success and failure

4.** Becoming a "Living Institution"- **When the individual's name becomes synonymous with the values of

the office.

“To find yourself, lose yourself in the service of others.” - **Mahatma Gandhi. **Devotion to duty is the **"alchemy" **that turns a bureaucrat into a public servant.

---

## Question 46 (Year: 2024 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2024-gs4-q46-civilsdaily**

**2024 - Mission Karmayogi is aiming for maintaining a very high standard of conduct and behaviour to ensure efficiency for serving citizens and in turn developing oneself. How will this scheme empower civil servants in enhancing productive efficiency and delivering the services at the grassroots level?** [Year: 2024] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**Mission Karmayogi (National Programme for Civil Services Capacity Building) **aims to transform the civil services from rule-based to role-based, competency-driven and citizen-centric administrative systems.

**Vision of civil servants**

**1. Imaginative & Innovative**

**2. Proactive & Polite**

**3. Professional & Progressive**

**4. Energetic & Enabling**

**5. Transparent & Tech-enabled**

**6. Creative & Constructive**

### Enhancing Productive Efficiency and Grassroots Service Delivery

1.** Shift to Role-based Governance **by mapping specific competencies to specific roles (FRAC) - ensures that the "right man is in the right job" .

2.** iGOT-Karmayogi Platform- **provides "anytime-anywhere" learning - allows a field officer in a remote district to access global best practices.

3.** Democratization of Training- **Karmayogi extends high-quality training to **Group B and C officials **who are the actual frontline of grassroots delivery.

4. It moves away from "one-time" training at the start of a career to a **continuous learning life-cycle, keeping officials updated on evolving technologies and laws.

5. Dedicated modules on **"Soft Skills" **empower officials to move from being "authorities" to "facilitators" - improves quality of citizen interaction at local offices.

6.** Common training modules **foster a **"Whole-of-Government" **approach - **breaks departmental silos**

7.** Evidence-based Training- **Using data analytics from the iGOT platform, the government can identify "competency gaps" in specific districts and deploy targeted training.

8. It creates a **uniform "Global Standard" of Indian civil service conduct, ensuring a citizen receives the same quality of service whether in Delhi or a tribal block.

9.** Public-Private Partnership in Content- **By curating content from global experts and private institutions, it brings **"Corporate Efficiency" **into the public sector mindset.

10.** Institutionalized Feedback- **Eg- **360-degree feedback mechanism**

11.** Focus on Emotional Intelligence (EI) **which is crucial for handling sensitive grassroots issues like land acquisition or communal harmony.

### Potential Challenges

1.** Digital Divide**

2.** Resistance to Change **(deep-rooted "Babu Culture")

3.** Language Barriers **for frontline staff.

4.** Weak incentives **- Learning not strongly linked to promotions.

5.** Infrastructure gaps **- Lack of devices for frontline workers.

6.** Over-standardisation **ignores local realities.

Effectively implemented, it can help build **citizen centric and future ready civil service **with right Attitude, Skills and Knowledge.

---

## Question 47 (Year: 2018 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2018-gs4-q47-civilsdaily**

**2018 - What is meant by conflict of interest? Illustrate with examples, the difference between the actual and potential conflicts of interest.** [Year: 2018] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

In public administration, a **Conflict of Interest (COI) **is a situation where the **private interests **of a public official clash with their **professional duties **and responsibilities.

**Manifestation of conflict of interest**

1.** Financial Investments **in companies regulated by one's own department.

2.** Family Ties (Nepotism). **Eg- Chanda Kochhar Case

3.** Post-Employment Ambitions (Revolving Door). **Eg- "Amakudari" in Japan

4.** Gifts and Hospitality**

5.** Outside Directorships**

6.** Personal Biases**

7.** Secondary Employment. Eg- Moonlighting**

8. **Property Interests**

**Actual vs. Potential Conflict of Interest**

| **Feature** | **Actual Conflict of Interest** | **Potential Conflict of Interest** |

| --- | --- | --- |

| **Definition** | A direct and current clash between duty and interest. | A situation where a conflict might arise in the future. |

| **Nature** | Real and existing | Foreseeable |

| **Legal Standing** | Usually a violation of conduct rules if not disclosed. | Not a violation yet, but requires a "management plan." |

| **Ethical**
**Standing** | Violation of duty and probity | Ethical risk requiring disclosure |

| **Public**
**Perception** | Seen as active corruption or bias. | Seen as a risk factor that needs monitoring. |

| **Action Needed** | **Recusal **(stepping down) or Divestment. | **Disclosure **(declaring the interest). |

| **Result** | Immediate compromise of objectivity. | Future risk of compromised objectivity. |

| **Example** | awarding a contract to a company owned by his spouse. | framing mining policy while owning mining stocks |

### Ways to Prevent Conflict of Interest

1.** Mandatory Disclosure of Assets **(2nd ARC)**

2.** Cooling-off Period**

3.** Code of Ethics and office of Ethics Commissioner**

4.** Institutionalized "Conflict of Interest" Registers**

5.** Integrity Pacts**

In a democracy, the **appearance of **integrity is as important as integrity itself. Moving from a **culture of secrecy to a culture of disclosure, can help maintain public trust in governance.

---

## Question 48 (Year: 2019 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2019-gs4-q48-civilsdaily**

**2019 - What do you understand by probity in governance? Based on your understanding of the term, suggest measures for ensuring probity in government.** [Year: 2019] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**Probity **is a multifaceted concept representing the quality of having **strong moral principles, absolute integrity, and uprightness in the discharge of public duties.

### Key Components of Probity

1.** Integrity- **Adherence to a strict moral and ethical code. E- Lal Bahadur Shastri

2.** Transparency- **Decisions and actions must be open to public scrutiny.

3.** Accountability- **Public servants must be answerable for their actions and omissions.

4.** Objectivity- **Decisions should be based on merit and evidence, free from bias or personal interest.

5.** Impartiality- **Acting without prejudice toward any particular group or individual.

6.** Avoiding conflict of interest **through disclosures and recusals

7.** Frugality- **Treating public money with more care than one's own

Ensuring probity requires a **"triple-lock" approach**- **Structural, **Procedural, and **Behavioral.

**1. Institutional and Legal Reforms**

- Ensuring the independence and resource-sufficiency of bodies like **Lokpal, Lokayukta **and **CVC**

- Rigorous implementation of the **Whistleblowers Protection Act.

- Empowering the **CAG **to conduct social audits and performance audits

- ** Adoption of the "Hong Kong Model" (ICAC) **to tackle corruption - three-pronged strategy of Investigation, Prevention, and Community Education

**2. Procedural and Technological Measures**

- ** E-Governance **to reduce human discretion and the "gatekeeper" effect. Eg- **GeM**

- ** Citizens’ Charters- **Mandating clear timelines for service delivery. Eg- SAKALA (Karnataka Guarantee of Services Act)

- Proactive disclosure under **Section 4 of the RTI Act **for transparency

- Mandatory and periodic declaration of **assets and liabilities by civil servants**

**3. Human Resource and Ethical Reforms**

- Moving beyond a "Rule-based" conduct code (what not to do) to a **"Value-based" code of ethics **(what to strive for) (2nd ARC).

- ** Competency-linked training **under **Mission Karmayogi **to ensure civil servants are not only skilled but also ethically grounded.

**4. Social and Political Measures**

- ** Legal backing to Social Audits. (Meghalaya Act)**

- Ensuring **transparency in electoral funding **to prevent the "quid-pro-quo" culture at top.

As pointed out by **PM Modi **in Independence Day speech, promoting **‘suchita, pardarshita and nishpakshata’ (probity, transparency and impartiality) **is essential for ‘Amrit Kaal’

---

## Question 49 (Year: 2023 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2023-gs4-q49-civilsdaily**

**2023 - ‘Probity is essential for an effective system of governance and socio-economic development.’ Discuss.** [Year: 2023] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**Probity **refers to integrity, uprightness and ethical conduct in public life, especially in the use of public power and resources.

“The strength of a nation lies not in its wealth but in the integrity of its institutions.”

### Importance of Probity for Governance Effectiveness

1.** Ensures optimal resource utilization- **Eg- **DBT **through JAM has saved over 3.5 lakh Cr.

2. Promotes **accountability and reduces corruption. **Eg- CAG audits of coal block allocation

3.** Rule of Law- **Probity ensures that laws are applied uniformly without selective enforcement. Eg- **T.N. Seshan **strictly enforced MCC

4.** Building Public Trust- **Integrity in public dealings enhances citizens' confidence in the state.

5.** Reducing Administrative "Red Tape"- **Probity eliminates the artificial delays created by officials to solicit "speed money." Eg- **MCA21 portal **for corporate filings

6.** Administrative Speed- **Ethical governance reduces internal friction and decision-paralysis. Eg- **E. Sreedharan **completed Delhi Metro ahead of schedule.

7.** Internal Motivation- **Probity fosters a "service-oriented" work culture rather than a "power-oriented" one.

8.** Prevention of "Elite Capture" **of policy through citizen participation and feedback. Eg- EIA

### Importance of Probity for Socio-Economic Development

1.** Attract Investment **due to a predictable and stable environment free from "hidden costs." Eg-**Singapore **attracts global capital because of its reputation for zero tolerance for bribery.

2.** Inclusive Growth (Antyodaya)- **Probity ensures that welfare schemes reach the "last person" in the queue.

3.** Human Capital Formation- **Merit-based recruitment improves the quality of the workforce. Eg- The **UPSC's **reputation for probity

4.** Sustainability- **Decisions made with probity consider long-term environmental impacts over short-term gains.

5.** Social Cohesion- **Fairness in governance prevents the grievances and conflicts that arise from perceived injustice.

6. Emphasis on **meritocracy and objectivity **is the engine of a modern, knowledge-based economy.

7.** Probity in judiciary **ensure accessibility, affordability and quality of justice - Promotes **Justice and Equality**

8.** Probity in corporate governance **promotes effective CSR under **trusteeship principle. Eg- **Project Nanhi Kali of Mahindra Group **for women education

**“The price of greatness is responsibility.” - Winston Churchill.**

Probity ensures that responsibility is exercised with integrity, fairness and public spirit.

---

## Question 50 (Year: 2024 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2024-gs4-q50-civilsdaily**

**2024 - “In Indian culture and value system, an equal opportunity has been provided irrespective of gender identity. The number of women in public service has been steadily increasing over the years.” Examine the gender-specific challenges faced by female public servants and suggest suitable measures to increase their efficiency in discharging their duties and maintaining high standards of probity.** [Year: 2024] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

From just **11.2% **of total IAS officers in 2011, the number of women has risen to nearly **15% **in 2022.

**"I measure the progress of a community by the degree of progress which women have achieved." **- **Dr. B.R. Ambedkar**

### Women in Indian Culture

1.** Shakti- **primordial source of power, energy.

2.** Ardhanarishvara Philosophy**

3.** Matrushakti- **Governance as caretaking.

4.** W**omen like Gargi and Maitreyi as public intellectuals and decision-makers in Sabhas.

### Gender-Specific Challenges Faced by Female Public Servants

1.** The "Double Burden" Syndrome- **Time Use Surveys show Indian women spend nearly **5 hours/day **on unpaid care work vs. 30 minutes for men.

2.** Glass Walls in Postings- **Systematic "pigeonholing" into departments like Education, Health, or Social Welfare, while being kept away from Finance, Home, or Infrastructure.

3.** The "Old Boys' Club" Exclusion- **Informal networking and decision-making often happen in "after-hours" social settings that are less accessible to women.

4.** Under-representation at senior levels **(“glass ceiling” effect)

5.** Infrastructure Gaps in Field Postings- **Lack of functional toilets or secure overnight accommodation in remote blocks.

6.** Perception of "Weakness"- **Subordinates or local political leaders in patriarchal pockets resist taking orders from a female officer.

7.** Safety and Harassment- **Subtle forms of workplace sexism and the threat of physical harm in law-and-order roles.

8.** The Mobility Penalty- **Frequent transfers are harder for women leading to "deputation" requests

9. Taking maternity leave is often viewed as a "loss of productivity," affecting seniority or key assignments.

10.** Tokenism- **appointed to committees merely to fulfill a "gender quota" rather than for expertise.

11.** Internalized Bias- **The pressure to over-perform to prove "toughness," which can lead to excessive **stress and burnout **compared to male peers.

### Measures to Increase Efficiency and Maintain Probity

1.** Institutionalizing Hybrid Work- **Following global best practices (Scandinavia)

2.** Strict POSH implementation with real enforcement - Functional ICCs, time-bound inquiries, protection from retaliation.**

3. Establishing **civil services board **for transparent transfers **(2nd ARC)**

4.** Mandatory Crèche Facilities **at every Secretariat and District Collectorate.

5.** Gender-sensitive infrastructure **- Eg- Standardised “safe field deployment” norms for night duty

6. Creating networks like the **"IAS Women's Association" **to provide juniors with strategies to handle political pressure and maintain probity.

7.** Sensitization- **Mandatory behavioral training through **Mission Karmayogi **to foster professional respect.

8.** Gender Budgeting in Administration- **For the professional development and safety requirements of female staff within departments.

The **"highest perfection" **in public service can only be achieved when the workforce is **truly representative**

---

## Question 51 (Year: 2023 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2023-gs4-q51-civilsdaily**

**2023 - In the context of the work environment, differentiate between ‘coercion’ and ‘undue influence’ with suitable examples.** [Year: 2023] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**Work culture **refers to the shared values, norms, behaviour and ethical climate that shape how individuals interact, make decisions and exercise authority within an organisation.

“The culture of any organisation is shaped by the worst behaviour the leader is willing to tolerate.”

| **Coercion** | **Undue Influence** |

| --- | --- |

| use of **force, threat, intimidation or punishment **to compel a person to act against their will. | use of **position, authority, relationship, persuasion or subtle pressure **to unfairly influence a person’s decision |

| Forceful compulsion through abuse or threat | Subtle manipulation through emotional means |

| Consent of employee is absent | Involves consent but is distorted |

| Open and explicit | Indirect and concealed |

| Clearly illegal. Eg- violation of POSH Act | Often unethical, legally grey |

| Intensity is high and immediate | Intensity is gradual and psychological |

| Mostly used through authority or hierarchy | Mostly leveraged by personal and emotional connections |

| Results in act under duress or whistleblowing or resignation | May face crisis of conscience or guilt |

| Remedy - Institutional and legal measures. Eg-ICC complaint | Remedy - Code of ethics and code of conduct |

| Violation of autonomy | Violation of fairness |

| Threat of transfer for not clearing illegal file | Hint of promotion for approving biased decision |

### Way Forward for a Healthy and Ethical Work Culture

1.** Institutionalizing 360-Degree Feedback**

2.** Strengthening Whistleblower Protection Mechanisms**

3.** Civil services board for transparent transfer and posting**

4.** Adopting Nolan Principles **of **openness**

5.** Promoting "Psychological Safety"**

6.** Regular Ethics Audits**

7.** Democratizing the Workplace**

**"Highest Perfection" **in duty can never be achieved through fear or manipulation. For effective work culture, authority must be exercised through **competence and trust**

---

## Question 52 (Year: 2023 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2023-gs4-q52-civilsdaily**

**2023 - Explain the term social capital. How does it enhance good governance?** [Year: 2023] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**Social capital **refers to the **networks, norms, values and trust **that enable individuals and groups to cooperate for mutual benefit and collective action.

"Social capital is the lubricant that makes the wheels of democracy turn."

According to political scientist **Robert Putnam, social capital consists of two main types-

- ** Bonding Social Capital- **Links between people of similar backgrounds (family, class).

- ** Bridging Social Capital- **Links between people from different groups.

### Role of Social Capital in Enhancing Good Governance

1.** Enhanced Accountability- **High social capital empowers citizens to monitor the government. Eg- high public participation in local government in kerala

2.** Reduction in Transaction Costs- **When trust is high, the government spends less on policing and litigation.

3.** Facilitating "Co-Production" of Services- **Eg- The **Bhagidari Scheme **in

Delhi involved RWAs in managing local water and electricity issues.

4.** Effective Grievance Redressal- **Strong social networks **amplify the voice of the marginalized. **Eg- **Kudumbashree **network in Kerala.

5.** Promoting "Bottom-Up" Planning- **Social capital makes the **Gram Sabha **a vibrant decision-making body. Eg- **people’s plan campaign in kerala**

6.** Reducing Conflict and Promoting Peace- **Eg- **Peace Committees **use inter-community trust to de-escalate tensions before they turn into riots.

7.** Behavioral Change (Nudge Theory)- **Social capital is the engine of **"Jan Andolan" **(People's Movements). Eg- success of **Pulse Polio **immunization.

8.** Improving Public Policy Compliance- **Eg- Higher **tax compliance **rates in countries where citizens perceive the "social contract" to be strong and fair.

9.** Inclusive Resource Management- **It prevents the "Tragedy of the Commons."

10.** Humanizing the Bureaucracy- **It bridges the gap between the "Ruler" and the "Ruled." Eg-**"Compassionate Kozhikode" **initiative by IAS Prasant Nair

**Ways to Build social capital**

1. Strengthening Grassroots Decentralization with 4F’s

2. Education for "Civic Virtue"

3. Institutionalizing Community Policing

4. Strengthening civil society as a “bridge”

5. Implementing "Social Audits" as a Norm

For India to move toward **"Minimum Government, Maximum Governance," **the state must act as a facilitator of social capital, transforming passive subjects into active, trusting, and responsible citizens.

---

## Question 53 (Year: 2018 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2018-gs4-q53-civilsdaily**

**2018 - “In doing a good thing, everything is permitted which is not prohibited expressly or by clear implication”. Examine the statement with suitable examples in the context of a public servant discharging his/her duties.** [Year: 2018] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

This statement reflects the principle of **Administrative Discretion **and **Innovation **in public service. It also highlights the shift from **"Rule-based" **to **"Goal-oriented" **governance.

**Everything is permitted in doing good thing**

1. Adherence to the utilitarian **principle of ‘greatest happiness.’**

2.** Resource optimization- **Eg- **Armstrong Pame (IAS) **crowdfunded the "People’s Road".

3.** Innovation for reformative justice- Kiran Bedi (IPS) **introduced Vipassana.

4.** Behavioral Nudging (Gandhigiri)- **Using psychology instead of force. Eg- In the **Swachh Bharat Abhiyan, officers gifted flowers to people defecating in the open.

5. Prioritising **social welfare **by bypassing bureaucratic rigidity. Eg- **Prashant Nair’s **"Operation Sulaimani" - Use of crowdsourced coupons to feed hunger

6. Finding **‘out of the box’ solutions. Eg- IPS **chetan singh Rathore **using National Anthem to manage protesting crowd.

7.** Ethical use of discretion in crises. Eg- **Dr. Syed Sehrish Asgar **used her office as a "human call center" during communication blackouts in J&K

8. Helps in **collaborative problem solving **rather than a top-down approach. Eg- S.R. Sankaran **involved local community elders in identifying bonded laborers.

9. Creativity and innovations facilitate **adoption of technology **to solve problems. Eg- **Dr. Hari Chandana **building pavements from recycled plastic in Hyderabad.

10.** Inaction **out of fear of rules is often a greater "evil" than **Innovation **within the framework of the law. -leads to **policy paralysis**

### Boundaries that Need to be Followed

1.** Constitutional Morality- **One cannot "do good" by violating

Fundamental Rights. Eg- unauthorized phone tapping.

2.** Financial Propriety- **Eg- following **due process **in tender allocation

3.** Avoiding Conflict of Interest **through declaration and recusal

4. Acting in the **"spirit" of the law**

5.** Dignity and Human Rights- **Adherence to Kant’s categorical imperative.

6.** Non-arbitrariness **- No favouritism under the garb of welfare.

The ultimate test for any "permitted" action is **Mahatma Gandhi's Talisman**- "Will it lead to the upliftment of the poorest?"

### Counter-Argument- The Risks of Unchecked Discretion

1. Erosion of Procedural Due Process- Eg- 2G spectrum case
2. Financial Irregularity and Corruption
3. "Rule of Men" over "Rule of Law." Eg- Bulldozer justice
4. Violation of Fundamental Rights- Eg- custodial torture
5. Policy Instability and Lack of Continuity
6. Risk of Political Misuse

**7. Moral Hazard **of **normalising shortcuts. **Eg- Illegal tapping to catch criminals.

8.** Accountability Gap may lead to institutional Decay**

9.** The "Savior Complex"- **can lead to administrative arrogance.

---

## Question 54 (Year: 2024 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2024-gs4-q54-civilsdaily**

**2024 - “Mindless addiction to Form, ignoring the Substance of the matter, results in rendering of injustice. A perceptive civil servant is one who ignores such literalness and carries out true intent.” Examine the above statement with suitable illustrations.** [Year: 2024] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

In public administration, there is tension between **procedural formalism **and **substantive justice. When it becomes a slave to "Form," it becomes an end in itself, at the cost of the citizen it was meant to serve.

### Mindless Addiction to Form- Rendering Injustice

1.** Institutionalization of Red Tapism- **Eg- **Munger-Ganga Bridge **in Bihar was delayed by nearly 14 years due to inter-departmental disputes

2. Literalness breeds a **"mechanical" mindset **where officials **lose empathy. **Eg- denial of emergency care to critically ill patient without documentation

3.** Inefficiency in crisis management- **Eg- migrant labour sufferings during COVID.

4.** Undermining Rights of the Vulnerable- **Eg- PDS exclusion of poor due to biometric authentication failures (Jharkhand case)

5.** Encourages moral abdication - **Officials transfer moral responsibility to the rulebook (banality of evil). Eg- encroachment demolitions without rehabilitation plan.

6. Facilitates **coercive corruption. Eg- ‘speed money’ for faster file clearance

7. Complexity of the "Form" leads to **Process becoming Punishment. Eg- **complexity in environmental clearances

8. "By-the-book" culture **stifles innovation and creativity.**

9.** Resource Wastage- **Eg- cost and time overruns in PPP projects due to delays in land procurement

10.** Policy Paralysis- **Fear of audit or the "3C" (CBI, CVC, CAG) leads to "Defensive Bureaucracy."

### The Perceptive Civil Servant- Carrying Out True Intent

1.** Prioritizing Humanitarian Spirit and constitutional morality. **Eg- **Dr. Syed Sehrish Asgar **used her office as a "human call center" during communication blackouts in J&K

2.** Proactive Problem-Solving in emergencies- **Eg-**Dr. Rajendra Bharud (IAS) **setting up an oxygen plant in tribal Nandurbar before the second COVID wave

3.** Empowering through Informal Networks- **Eg**Armstrong Pame (IAS) **built a 100km road via crowdfunding.

4.** Administrative Empathy for the Marginalized- **EgIn the **"Project Sulaimani" **model (Kozhikode), the "Substance" of dignity was prioritized.

5.** Reforming through Discretion- **Eg- **Kiran Bedi (IPS) **turned Tihar Jail into a reformatory.

6.** Streamlining Processes for the Citizen- **Perceptive officers redesign the "Form" itself. **DM of Ganjam (Vijay Kulange) **institutionalized "Doorstep Delivery" of pensions for the disabled

7.** Innovative problem solving- **Eg- **Rahul Kumar (IAS) **converted abandoned buildings into libraries using maintenance funds.

8.** Defending the Rights of the Voiceless- **Eg- **S. Sankaran (IAS) **provided instant subsistence relief to rescued bonded laborers.

Rules are meant to serve justice and when they fail to do so, conscience must guide discretion.

---

## Question 55 (Year: 2022 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2022-gs4-q55-civilsdaily**

**2022 - Wisdom lies in knowing what to reckon with and what to overlook. An officer being engrossed with the periphery, ignoring the core issues before him, is no rare in the bureaucracy. Do you agree that such preoccupation of an administrator leads to travesty of justice to the cause of effective service delivery and good governance? Critically evaluate.** [Year: 2022] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

When a civil servant becomes a slave to periphery or "form," administration becomes an end in itself, at the cost of the citizen it was meant to serve.

**Core Vs Periphery**

| **The Core (Substance)** | **The Periphery (Form)** |

| --- | --- |

| Ensuring **Justice **and **Dignity. | Excessive **Documentation **and **Rules. |

| **Solving the Problem **at hand. | Following the **Standard Operating Procedure. |

| **Spirit of the Law. | **Letter of the Law. |

| **Outcome-Oriented **Governance. | **Process-Oriented **Bureaucracy. |

**Preoccupation with periphery - travesty of justice**

1.** Red-tapism over responsiveness- **Eg- **Munger-Ganga Bridge **in Bihar was delayed by nearly 14 years due to inter-departmental disputes

2. It is a **"corruption of omission"**- may be legally clean, but ethically bankrupt.

3. Periphery breeds a **"mechanical" mindset **where officials **lose empathy. **Eg- denial of emergency care to critically ill patient without documentation

4.** Process compliance over public welfare. Eg- Eg- PDS exclusion of poor due to biometric authentication failures (Jharkhand case)

5.** Encourages moral abdication - **Officials transfer moral responsibility to the rulebook (banality of evil). Eg- encroachment demolitions without rehabilitation plan.

6. Facilitates **coercive corruption. Eg- ‘speed money’ for faster file clearance

7. It leads to **Process becoming Punishment. Eg- **complexity in environmental clearances

8. "By-the-book" culture **stifles innovation and creativity.**

9.** Resource Wastage- **Eg- cost and time overruns in PPP projects due to delays in land procurement

10.** Policy Paralysis- **Fear of audit or the "3C" (CBI, CVC, CAG) leads to "Defensive Bureaucracy."

### Way Forward

1.** Adopting the "Karmayogi" Mindset- **"solution-providers" rather than "file-pushers".

**Vision of civil servants**

**1. Imaginative & Innovative**

**2. Proactive & Polite**

**3. Professional & Progressive**

**4. Energetic & Enabling**

**5. Transparent & Tech-enabled**

**6. Creative & Constructive**

2.** Institutionalizing Social Audits- **Eg- Meghalaya social audit law

3.** Protection for Honest Discretion **by amending Section 17A of the Prevention of Corruption Act.

4.** Promoting "Co-Production"- **Involving NGOs and SHGs to deliver services. Eg- **Kudumbashree**

5.** Application of Gandhi’s Talisman **in decision making

The ultimate goal of an administrator is to ensure that the **"True Intent" **of the Constitution - Justice, Liberty, and Equality - is delivered.

---

## Question 56 (Year: 2025 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2025-gs4-q56-civilsdaily**

**2025 - “For any kind of social re-engineering by successfully implementing welfare schemes, a civil servant must use reason and critical thinking in an ethical framework.” Justify this statement with suitable examples.** [Year: 2025] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

Social re-engineering refers to the deliberate attempt to **transform social structures, behaviors, and cultural norms **to achieve a more **equitable society. Civil servants act as a **“facilitator” **of this change.

### Need for reason and critical thinking in an ethical framework for successful social engineering

1.** Diagnose real problems, not symptoms **- Eg- Nutrition deficits need diet diversity, not only calories.

critic^
p^sern^S

2.** Build public trust and legitimacy. Eg- Transparent DBT reduced leakage and improved targeting.

Epical f paro^0^

3. Uphold **constitutional morality over social morality. **Eg-**conditional cash transfer **under **"Kanyashree" **scheme improved efficiency.

4.** Design context-specific solutions. Eg- Jal Jeevan Mission adapted to local water sources.

5.** Avoid one-size-fits-all policies. Eg- location specific housing designs under PM Awas.

6.** Prevent unintended harm. Eg- advising against loan waivers to avoid moral hazard.

7.** Balancing competing values. Eg- balancing efficiency and privacy in Aadhaar.

8.** Ensure bottoms up planning. Eg- fair, prior and informed consent of Gram Sabha under PESA.

9.** Prevent elite capture **of policy. Eg- Social audits in MGNREGA.

10.** Promote behavioural change, not just compliance. Eg- Gandhigiri in SBM - giving flowers for open defecation.

11.** Ensure sustainability **(intergenerational justice). Eg- **PM-PRANAM **to promote organic farming

12.** Protect rights while delivering welfare. Eg- Consent-based data use in health IDs.

Social transformation requires **critical reasoning to design effective interventions and ethical grounding to ensure justice, dignity and inclusion.

## Question 57 (Year: 2025 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2025-gs4-q57-civilsdaily**

**2025 - To achieve holistic development goal, a civil servant acts as an enabler and active facilitator of growth rather than a regulator. What specific measures will you suggest to achieve this goal?** [Year: 2025] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

“The civil servant is not a mere tool of the government; he is a servant of the people.” - **C. Rajagopalachari **For **Viksit Bharat, **civil services needs to shift from “weberian” rule-based bureaucracy to “democratic” and enabling bureaucracy.

### Holistic Development Goals

1.** Economic Inclusivity **(Antyodaya).

2.** Gender Equality**

3.** Environmental Sustainability**

4.** Human Capital development**

5.** Ease of Living**

**6. Good governance**

**7. Social harmony**

**Civil servant as regulator vs enabler**

| **Civil Servant as a Regulator** | **Civil Servant as an Enabler** |

| --- | --- |

| Focus on compliance | Driving growth and fostering innovation. |

| **Rule-based** | **Role-based** |

| Command and Control model (Top-down) | Collaborative mindset (participatory) |

| Reactive | Proactive |

### Measures needed

1. Promoting “**Ease of compliance**” and reducing "time-tax" on entrepreneurs and citizens. Eg- **"Deemed Approvals" and Single Windows (Bibek Debroy Committee)**

2.** Attitudinal Transformation **through **"Mission Karmayogi" - **From **Mai-Baap (patronizing) **culture toward a **citizen-first approach.

3.** Institutionalizing Participatory Governance- **Eg- **Participatory Budgeting **model of Porto Alegre, Brazil

4.** Strengthening Public-Private-Community Partnerships (PPCP)- **Eg- In **Kudumbashree **in Kerala, civil servants facilitate growth by empowering 4.5 million women to run micro-enterprises.

5.** Data-Driven Decision Making- **Eg- **Aspirational Districts Programme **uses a real-time dashboard to rank districts - make DM as **competitive facilitator **of local development.

6.** Adopting "Nudge Theory" for Social Engineering. **Eg- **Swachh Bharat Abhiyan **succeeded because of community persuasion rather than just fining them for open defecation.

7.** Promoting Frugal Innovation- **Encouraging officers to solve local problems with available resources.

8.** Safeguarding "Honest Discretion"**by amending **Section 17A of the Prevention of Corruption Act**

9.** Facilitating "Last Mile" Digital Service Delivery **through **Common Service Centres (CSCs)**

This can help civil servants become an enabler that unlocks the **productive potential **of citizens, markets and communities.

## Question 58 (Year: 2022 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2022-gs4-q58-civilsdaily**

**2022 - Whistle blower, who reports corruption and illegal activities, wrongdoing and misconduct to the concerned authorities, runs the risk of being exposed to grave danger, physical harm and victimization by the vested interests, accused persons and his team. What policy measures would you suggest to strengthen the protection mechanism to safeguard the whistle blower?** [Year: 2022] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

A whistleblower is described as the **"conscience of the organization." **They are individuals who, out of a sense of public duty, report corruption and misconduct within an organization to competent authorities. **Risks faced by whistle blower**

1.** Leak of identity - Eg- Satyendra Dubey’s **identity was leaked despite his request for anonymity to the PMO.

1.** Violent Assault and Murder- S. Manjunath (2005), an IOCL officer, was shot dead.

2.** Unnatural Deaths- **In the **Vyapam Scam, nearly 40 people died under suspicious circumstances.

3.** Institutional Victimization- **transferred to remote postings repeatedly to break their morale.

4.** False Disciplinary Inquiries **on fabricated charges of insubordination or breach of conduct.

5.** Social Ostracization- **labeled as "snitches" or "disloyal".

6.** Economic Harassment- **withholding promotions, denying increments etc.

7.** Legal Entrapment **under the **official secrets Act (1923)**

### Policy Measures to Strengthen the Protection Mechanism

1.** Strict "Anonymity by Design"- **Eg- encrypted digital portal for reporting

2.** Criminalizing the Leak of Identity**

3.** Proactive Threat Assessment **to provide immediate security or relocation.

4.** Financial Incentives (Bounty System)- **Following the **U.S. False Claims Act, whistleblowers should be entitled to a percentage of the money recovered from the exposed scam.

5. Protection must extend to **private sector employees and contractors, as corruption often involves **public-private nexuses.

6.** Time-Bound Investigation **to minimize the "exposure time" of the complainant.

7.** Whistleblower Defense Fund **to provide legal aid and psychological counseling.

8.** Witness Protection Programs- **"Relocation and Identity Change" services for whistleblowers and their families.

9. Establishing **"Integrity Awards" **(potentially awarded anonymously or post-retirement) to change the social narrative from "snitching" to "patriotism."

10.** Providing job security **and protection against **"Victimization" **through **independent **ombudsman

A whistleblower is a vital cog in the machinery of **Good Governance. Their safety is essential to maintain **probity **in administration.

---

**Question ID: 2023-gs4-q59-civilsdaily**

**2023 - “Corruption is the manifestation of the failure of core values in the society.” In your opinion, what measures can be adopted to uplift the core values in the society?** [Year: 2023] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

Corruption is the abuse of entrusted power for private gain, resulting in distortion of justice, fairness and public interest.

### Corruption as the manifestation of failure of core values

**1. Erosion of integrity**

**2. Decline of responsibility**

THE WHEEL OF CORRUPTION

**3. Weak public spirit**

**4. Normalization of unethical behaviour (sanskritization)**

**5. Loss of respect for law**

**6. Materialism over morality**

**7. Breakdown of accountability**

**8. Greed over Contentment**

**9. Loss of Professional Ethics**

**10. Materialism over Spirituality/Humanism**

### Measures to uplift core values in society

1.** Value-based education **- Ethics and civic education in schools.

2.** Family and community socialisation **- Teaching honesty at home.

3.** Media responsibility **- Highlighting integrity

stories, not just scandals.

4.** Reward ethical behaviour **- Public recognition of whistleblowers.

5.** Transparent governance **- Eg- DBT has saved over 3.5 lakh Cr of government

6.** Civic participation **- Social audits and RTI activism.

7.** Cultural reinforcement **- Films and literature celebrating moral courage.

8.** Swift and certain punishment **under Prevention of Corruption Act and Fast-track courts to end the "culture of impunity."

9. Utilizing spiritual leaders to preach **"Aparigraha" **(non-attachment) and **"Asteya" **(non-stealing).

10. Breaking **politician-bureaucrat-civil servant nexus (Vohra committee)**

    **a. Transparency in political funding**

    **b. Civil services board **for transparent postings and transfers

By fostering **integrity, empathy, and public spirit, we can move from a society of "Rules" to a society of

"Character," where corruption finds no soil to take root.

## Question 60 (Year: 2019 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2019-gs4-q60-civilsdaily**

**2019 - There is a view that the Official Secrets Act is an obstacle to the implementation of Right to Information Act. Do you agree with this view? Discuss.** [Year: 2019] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

The OSA is a pre-independence law designed to **protect state secrets from "enemy states.**" The RTI Act is a **rights-based legislation **aimed at empowering citizens to **hold the government accountable.**

**OSA as an obstacle to RTI**

**1. Broad and vague definition of “secret” - **Routine administrative files marked confidential to **avoid scrutiny and undermine openness**

**2. Fear of criminal liability - **Officials hesitate to disclose information fearing prosecution under OSA.

**3. Over-classification - **Even non-sensitive data is labelled confidential to prevent disclosure.

**4. Used as a shield against accountability - **OSA invoked to deny information on public interest matters. Eg- allegations of corruption in **Rafale deal **but information not shared.

**5. Chilling effect on whistle-blowers and journalists - **Fear of prosecution discourages exposure of wrongdoing.

**6. Conflicts with RTI’s spirit of maximum disclosure (Section 4)**

**7. Lack of independent review of classification - **No strong mechanism to challenge unjustified secrecy.

8.** Psychological Barrier- **The OSA fosters a "default-to-secrecy" mindset.

### Need of OSA

**1. Protects national security and sovereignty**

**2. Safeguards strategic negotiations - **Trade, defence and foreign policy talks need confidentiality.

**3.** Section 8 of RT protects security-related information.

4. Certain **internal reports **on communal or ethnic tensions are kept secret to prevent the sparking of riots or civil unrest.

A separate National Security Act as suggested by 2nd ARC is needed to promote the culture of transparency and openness

---

## Question 61 (Year: 2018 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2018-gs4-q61-civilsdaily**

**2018 - “The Right to Information Act is not all about citizens’ empowerment alone, it essentially redefines the concept of accountability. Discuss.** [Year: 2018] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

The RTI Act, 2005, is celebrated as the "**Sunshine Legislation" **aims to promote **“informed citizenry" **and transform bureaucratic culture from **"secrecy and command" **to **"transparency and answerability." RTI as a Tool for Citizen Empowerment**

1.** Direct Questioning of Power**

2.** Rights based approach**

3.** Voice to voiceless**

4.** Informed political participation**

5.** Protection of Human Rights **(RTI on custodial deaths or condition of prisons)

6.** Bridge to Other Rights (Right to food under NFSA)**

### RTI redefining accountability

**1. From vertical to horizontal accountability - **direct accountability to citizens.

2.** Ending "Bureaucratic Anonymity"- **Eg- RTI makes file

notings public, ensuring accountability of specific officers taking decisions.

**3. From discretionary secrecy to mandatory disclosure - **reverses the presumption of secrecy to presumption of openness. Eg- **Adarsh Housing Scam **exposure

**4. From reactive to proactive accountability - **Section 4 mandates suo motu disclosure, making accountability continuous.

**5. From procedural to outcome accountability - **Citizens question not just rules but results.

**6. From internal audit to social audit - **People become auditors of governance. Eg- **MKSS in Rajasthan **used **Jan Sunwai **to expose fake work entries in MGNREGA.

**7. From elite oversight to mass oversight - **Every citizen becomes a watchdog.

**8. From episodic scrutiny to real-time scrutiny - **Continuous public monitoring through RTI queries.

**9. From moral accountability to legal accountability - **Failure to disclose invites penalties.

**10. From opacity-based power to transparency-based legitimacy - **Authority now depends on openness. Eg- **2G Spectrum and Coal Scams **exposure

**Issues**

1. Over **4 lakh appeals **are pending.

2. Chronic **Vacancies **in Commissions

3. Clash with OSA and DPDP Act

4. Legislative Dilution (2019 Amendment)

5. Safety and Threats to Activists (over 150 activists killed)

6. Poor Record Management

To ensure that the RTI Act does not become a **"dead letter" law, the focus must shift from mere legal compliance to a culture of **proactive transparency.

---

## Question 62 (Year: 2019 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2019-gs4-q62-civilsdaily**

**2019 - Explain the basic principles of the citizens charter movement and bring out its importance.** [Year: 2019] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

The **Citizen’s Charter, introduced in India in **1997 (DARPG) **following the **UK model, aims to make public services **transparent, accountable, and citizen-centric **by clearly defining service standards, timelines, and grievance redressal mechanisms.

### Basic Principles of the Citizens' Charter Movement

1.** Standards: **Explicitly state the **quality and level of service **citizens can expect, ideally with **specific, measurable timeframes.**

2.** Quality: **Commit to **continuously improving the standard **of services provided to meet user expectations.

3.** Choice: **Offer citizens a variety of **choices and options when accessing services, **wherever feasible.

4.** Transparency: **Ensure **openness in rules, procedures, schemes, **and grievance redress mechanisms.

5.** Accountability: **Hold individual officials and organizations **answerable for the services delivered **and commitments made.

6.** Value: **Ensure that services provide good value **for taxpayers' money.**

### Importance of citizen charters

1.** Defines Service Standards - Eg- **Passport Seva Kendra specifies delivery within **3 working days **for Tatkal applications.

2.** Enhances Administrative Transparency - **Makes **procedures, responsibilities, and timelines public, reducing scope for arbitrariness and discretion.

3.** Promotes Accountability of Officials - **Identifies **responsible officers **for each service and grievance redressal, ensuring **answerability for delays or failures.

4.** Empowers Citizens **to **demand better service delivery, question inefficiencies, and seek **grievance redressal **through defined channels.

5. Builds **mutual expectations **between government and citizens, enhancing trust in public institutions.

6. Provides a **benchmark for assessing departmental efficiency **and monitoring service outcomes through periodic audits.

7. Promotes feedback-based improvement by institutionalizing citizen input in service reforms.

**Case Studies**

1.** Indian Railways: **compensation, cleanliness standards, and punctuality targets.

2.** Taxpayers’ Charter: **Defines rights like privacy and fair treatment.

By aligning it with the **2nd ARC recommendations, it can evolve from a symbolic commitment to a **practical framework for responsive, transparent, and citizen-centric governance.

---

## Question 63 (Year: 2021 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2021-gs4-q63-civilsdaily**

**2021 - An independent and empowered social audit mechanism is an absolute must in every sphere of public service, including judiciary, to ensure performance, accountability and ethical conduct. Elaborate.** [Year: 2021] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

A social audit is a democratic process where citizens directly review, evaluate, and verify the official records, expenditures, and actual field performance of public service institutions.

### Importance to Improve Performance of Public Service

1.** Optimizes Resource Utilization: **Eg: social audits under **MGNREGA **reduced leakages and improved rural asset quality in Andhra Pradesh

2.** Enhances Service Delivery Timelines: **Pressure from community monitoring forces officials to complete projects without bureaucratic delays.

3.** Improves Project Target Accuracy: **Eg: Verification drives under the **National Food Security Act **removed thousands of fake ration cards.

4.** Boosts Quality Standards: **Eg: Public scrutiny of rural school buildings and mid-day meals improves safety.

5.** Bridges Local Governance Gaps: **Community audits identify specific, missing civic amenities that top-down government planning often misses.

6.** Improves Judicial Case Management: **Citizen reviews of court functioning encourage registries to clear administrative delays and bottlenecks.

### Importance to Improve Accountability of Public Service

1.** Dismantles Bureaucratic Financial Opacity: **Eg: **Mazdoor Kisan Shakti Sangathan (MKSS) **pioneered public hearings to expose hidden corruption.

2.** Enforces Strict Consequence Mechanisms: **Clear evidence gathered during community audits forces authorities to penalize errant, corrupt officers.

3.** Checks Judicial Pendency Patterns: **Reviewing administrative timelines makes institutional court registries strictly accountable for systemic listing delays.

4.** Restricts Executive Fund Diversions: **Eg: Strict auditing of specialized **Scheduled Caste Sub-Plan **funds prevent diversion to general projects.

5.** Empowers Marginalized Civic Groups: **Social audits give institutional platforms to poor citizens to question powerful government decision-makers.

6.** Validates Right to Information: **Social audits turn passive information requests into an active, collective tool for community justice.

7.** Reduces Public Service Grievance Backlogs: **Institutionalizing community verification forces departments to quickly resolve long-pending public utility complaints.

### Importance to Improve Ethical Conduct

1.** Institutionalizes Public Service Integrity: **Regular public scrutiny conditions state officials to perform duties with high honesty and fairness.

2.** Discourages Conflict of Interest: **Public disclosure of project details prevents officials from giving lucrative contracts to relatives.

3.** Maintains High Judicial Ethics: **Reviewing court administration standards encourages judges to strictly follow codes of ethical conduct.

4.** Protects Citizen Dignity Rights: **Equal opportunity during public hearings prevents officials from displaying discriminatory caste or gender biases.

5.** Promotes Empathy in Administration: **Direct interactions with poor citizens during audits sensitive bureaucrats toward urgent field realities.

6.** Fosters Values of Truthfulness: **Eg: Stopping fraudulent documentation of ghost beneficiaries. Implementing independent social audits across all public spheres, including the judiciary, is vital to achieving absolute transparency, institutional integrity, and democratic governance.

---

## Question 64 (Year: 2019 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2019-gs4-q64-civilsdaily**

**2019 - What is meant by ‘crisis of conscience’? How does it manifest itself in the public domain?** [Year: 2019] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

A **crisis of conscience **is a situation where an individual experiences an intense internal conflict between their deep-seated moral values and the actions they are pressured to take or have already taken. **Manifestation in the Public Domain**

1.** Whistleblowing against Corruption**conflict between "loyalty to the organization" and "duty to the public" triggers a crisis.

2.** Implementation of Unjust Policies-**

Eg- implementing order for eviction of slum dwellers during a harsh winter without a rehabilitation plan.

3.** Conflict between Rule of Law and Compassion- **Eg- Denying a starving,

elderly woman her rations because her biometrics failed to authenticate.

4.** Political Pressure on Neutrality- **Eg- An officer being asked to manipulate environmental impact data to favor an industrial project.

5.** Medical Ethics in Public Healthcare- **Eg- Medical triage decisions

6.** Journalists **reporting on sensitive issues like human rights violations face a clash between **"patriotism" and "truth."**

7.** Environmental Protection vs. Development- **Eg- **Aarey Forest case **in Mumbai

8.** Institutional loyalty vs public interest- **When statisticians are pressured to "under-report" inflation or unemployment figures to suit a government’s narrative.

9.** Confidentiality vs. Public Safety- **When an official knows a "state secret" that involves a threat to public health but is ordered to remain silent.

10.** Efficiency vs justice **or Speedy action vs due process. Eg- Bulldozer demolitions.

11.** Security vs rights **- Eg- Internet shutdowns in J&K

12.** Career risk vs ethical stand **- Eg- **Sanjiv Chaturvedi (IFS) **facing transfers for exposing corruption in AIIMS and HRD Ministry.

13.** Majoritarian demand vs minority rights **- Public pressure conflicting with constitutional morality. Eg-Sabrimala case

### Ethical Framework to Address Crisis of Conscience

1.** Constitutional Morality**

2.** The Public Interest Test**

3.** Gandhian Talisman**

4.** Principle of Non-Maleficence**

5.** Objectivity and Neutrality**

6.** Transparency and Accountability**

7.** Courage of Conviction**

8.** Categorical Imperative (Kant)**

9.** Integrity (Wholeness)**

10.** Seeking Guidance through "Phronesis"**

“There is a higher court than courts of justice and that is the court of conscience. It supersedes all other courts.” - **Mahatma Gandhi**

By aligning actions with the **"higher court of conscience," **a public official can ensure **human-centric, just, and truly democratic **governance.**

---

## Question 65 (Year: 2023 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2023-gs4-q65-civilsdaily**

**2023 - Is conscience a more reliable guide when compared to laws, rules and regulations in the context of ethical decision making ? Discuss.** [Year: 2023] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

**Conscience **is the "inner voice" or the internal moral sense of what is right or wrong in one's conduct. “There is a higher court than courts of justice and that is the court of conscience. It supersedes all other courts.” - **Mahatma Gandhi Conscience as a Reliable Guide**

1. Conscience addresses the **"spirit" of justice **where the "letter" of the law may be silent, outdated, or inhumane. Eg- Civil disobedience movement by **Gandhiji**

2.** Addressing the "Legal Vacuum"- **Laws cannot predict every future scenario. In these situations, conscience is the only navigator.

1.** Humanizing**

**Bureaucracy- **While rules are rigid, conscience provides the empathy needed for substantive justice.

2.** Upholding Scientific Responsibility- **Eg- **Robert Oppenheimer **faced crisis of conscience after the atomic bomb's use, leading him to advocate for international nuclear control.

3.** Whistleblowing against Corporate Fraud (moral courage) - **Eg- **Sherron Watkins **exposed the Enron scandal.

4.** Guide for social and legal reforms- **Eg- **Martin Luther King’s **fight for Civil Rights Act.

5.** Environmental Stewardship- **Laws often lag behind ecological destruction. Eg- **Sunderlal Bahuguna **led the Chipko Movement based on a conscience-driven duty to protect nature.

6.** Integrity in Sports ("fair play") - Eg- Sachin Tendulkar walking off before the umpire gives a decision.

7.** Handling Political Pressure- **Eg- **Ashok Khemka **has prioritized his conscience over political convenience, resulting in over 50 transfers.

8. In **conflict zones **where local laws are absent, conscience remains the sole guide. Eg- **Malala Yousafzai**’s campaign for girls' education despite Taliban ban.

9.** Prevents moral blindness. Eg- Oskar Schindler saved Jews despite Nazi laws.

### Challenges with conscience as a guide

1.** Subjectivity. Eg- Extremists justify violence as moral duty.

2.** Cultural bias. Eg- Honour killings defended as conscience by communities.

3.** Moral relativism. Eg- Different consciences produce conflicting actions.

4.** Conflict with rule of law. Eg- Mob lynching violates “justice as fairness”

5.** Inconsistency**- Personal morals change across time and contexts.

6.** The "Slippery Slope"- **Once an official starts bypassing rules for "good" reasons, it becomes easier to bypass them for "convenient" or "bad" reasons later.

### Synthesis of Law and Conscience

1.** Constitutional morality as the bridge **- Align personal conscience with constitutional values like justice, liberty and equality.

2.** Ethics training for public officials **under Mission **Karmayogi.**

3. Updation of laws with evolving ethical standards. Eg- DPDP Act

4.** Discretion **should be subject to transparency and review.

5.** Institutional ethical safeguards **- Ethics committees, ombudsmen and judicial oversight The synthesis of the two can create a "Compassionate State."

---

## Question 66 (Year: 2021 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2021-gs4-q66-civilsdaily**

**2021 - Impact of digital technology as a reliable source of input for rational decision making is a debatable issue. Critically evaluate with suitable examples.** [Year: 2021] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

“Technology is a useful servant but a dangerous master.” - **Christian Lous Lange**

Digital technology provides vast data infrastructure for modern governance, yet its reliability as an input for objective, rational decision-making remains highly controversial.

### Digital Technology as a Reliable Source of Input for Rational Decision-Making

1.** Real-Time Policy Inputs: **Eg: CoWIN platform enabled real-time vaccine inventory planning across all Indian districts.

2.** Citizen Participation in Policy- **Eg- MyGov collected over 10 crore citizen suggestions that shaped the National Education Policy 2020.

3.** Digitizing demographic and macro-surveys **significantly eliminates human enumeration mistakes and calculation errors.

4.** Satellite tracking and geospatial maps **provide precise objective inputs for infrastructure projects. Eg: PM GatiShakti National Master Plan GIS data.

5.** Leakage Elimination- **Digital systems make welfare delivery accurate and eliminate corruption effectively. Eg- DBT transferred over ₹44 lakh crore and saved ₹3.48 lakh crore

6. Interlinked digital architectures **unify isolated departmental databases **into a singular, holistic policy-making dashboard. Helps eliminate duplication.

7.** Predictive Weather Planning: **Eg: The IMD's advanced Doppler radar systems supplying precise cyclone trajectory inputs to save coastal communities.

### Counter-Argument: The Flaws and Risks of Digital Inputs

1.** Poor data collection **practices hampers objective policy making and implementation. Eg- Ghost Beneficiaries under Ayushman Bharat.

2.** The "Black Box" Problem- **AI logic is often opaque.

3.** Institutionalizing Historical Bias- **If data is biased , the AI will "learn" and automate that bias. Eg- **US COMPAS tool biased against African-Americans.**

4.** Difficulty in ensuring accountability **for mistakes.

5.** Correlation vs Causation Fallacies: **Analytical engines can link two completely unrelated data trends together, generating irrational choices.

6.** Exclusion of the Digitally Illiterate **from policy making & online grievance portals

### Way Forward

1.** Human-in-the-Loop (HITL)- **The final "sign-off," especially in cases affecting human rights, must be by a human officer.

2. Mandating **regular 3rd-party audits **of government algorithms to detect and "unlearn" biases.

3.** The EU AI Act Approach- "Risk-Based Framework" **where high-risk AI (policing or judiciary) face the highest level of ethical regulation.

4.** Digital Ethics Commissions **including ethicists, jurists, and technologists to oversee AI deployment in public service.

5.** Ethical Coding Standards- **Teaching **"Ethics by Design" **to programmers working on public infrastructure.

While digital technology streamlines administrative efficiency, it cannot replace human empathy, requiring a balanced model where data informs but conscience rules.

---

## Question 67 (Year: 2022 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2022-gs4-q67-civilsdaily**

**2022 - What do you understand by term ‘good governance’? How far recent initiatives in terms of e-Governance steps taken by the State have helped the beneficiaries? Discuss with suitable examples.** [Year: 2022] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

“In the happiness of his people lies the king's happiness, in their welfare his welfare”. **-Kautilya**

**Good governance **is an administrative approach defined by transparency, accountability, responsiveness, equity, and inclusiveness.

### Core Principles of Good Governance (UNDP)

1.** Participation: **Direct/indirect citizen involvement in decision-making. Eg: Gram Sabhas.

2.** Rule of Law: **Fair legal frameworks enforced impartially. Eg: Independent judiciary.

3.** Transparency: **Free flow of accessible information. Eg: Mandatory disclosures under the RTI.

4.** Responsiveness: **Institutions serving stakeholders within timeframes. Eg: Citizens’ Charters and CPGRAMS grievance portal.

5.** Consensus Orientation: **Eg: Federal consensus in GST Council meetings.

6.** Equity/Inclusiveness: **Ensuring all members feel valued. Eg: PM Jan Dhan Yojana’s universal financial inclusion.

7.** Effectiveness/Efficiency: **Optimizing resources for societal needs. Eg: Direct Benefit Transfer (DBT) reducing subsidy leakages.

8.** Accountability: **Answerability of officials to the public. Eg: Mandatory CAG audits of government spending.

**Success of Recent E-Governance Initiatives**

1.** Eliminating Welfare Leakages- **Eg- DBT transferred over ₹44 lakh crore and saved ₹3.48 lakh crore by plugging leakages in subsidies.

2.** Paperless Document Access- **Eg- **DigiLocker **crossing 67.63 crore registered users, hosting over 950 crore verified digital documents.

3.** Telemedicine Reaching Remote Areas- **Eg- The **eSanjeevani platform **providing digital medical services to over 45.42 crore remote patients.

4.** Real-Time Payment and Financial Inclusion- **Eg- **Unified Payments Interface (UPI) **registering over 21.7 billion transactions worth ₹28.33 lakh crore in January 2026 alone.

5.** Democratization of Digital Commerce: **Eg: The **Open Network for Digital Commerce (ONDC) **supporting over 1.16 lakh retail sellers across 630 cities.

6.** Unified Public Grievance Redressal: **Eg: The **UMANG App **offering citizens smooth, singular access to over 1,700 diverse public utility services.

7.** Scientific Grassroots Nutrition Monitoring: **Eg: The **POSHAN Tracker **continuously monitoring nutrition metrics for 8.9 crore children in 14.03 lakh Anganwadi centers.

**Major limitations**

1.** Aadhaar-Linked Service Failures- Eg: Santoshi Kumari (11) starvation death **in Simdega, Jharkhand (2017)

2.** The Persistence of Digital Divide: Only 38% of rural households **have high-speed broadband vs. 85% in urban clusters.

3.** Digital Illiteracy: **only 38% rural population digitally literate. **Eg: Dependence on "CSC Middlemen" **for simple tasks like PM-Kisan registration due to UI/UX complexity.

4.** Linguistic Barriers: Eg: Despite "Bhashini," **real-time voice-to-text accuracy in tribal dialects (like Santhali or Gondi) remains below 60%.

5.** Digital gender gap: **Only 37% of Indian women have adopted mobile internet and only 26% use it regularly. (UNDP).

6.** Aadhaar exclusion: **A 2017 starvation death in Jharkhand's Simdega due to Aadhaar-linked ration card failure exposed authentication risks.

7.** Bureaucratic Resistance: **Lower-level officials often view e-governance as a threat to their discretionary power.

8.** Manpower & Skill Gaps: Eg: Dependence on private consultants **for maintaining critical state data centers (SDCs).

7.** Cybersecurity Threats: CERT-In reported 2.94 million cyber incidents **in 2025, specifically targeting state-owned utility grids.

### Way Forward

1. Enact a **National e-Governance Act **to make digital service delivery a mandatory right rather than an administrative choice.

2.** Accelerate BharatNet completion: **Connect remaining 55,000 GPs and 3.8 lakh non-GP villages by 2026 under Amended BharatNet Programme

3. Strengthen **Common Service Centres **as "Digital Post Offices." **Eg- Rajasthan’s e-Mitra **model

4.** Adopt X-Road interoperability layer (Estonia): **handles 2.7 billion data queries with "once-only" principle - citizen submits info only once. 99% services online.

5.** Implement 2nd ARC's 11th Report fully:**

    a. Adopt national "enterprise architecture" framework

    b. Mandatory Business Process Re-engineering before digitisation;

    c. Build SMART (Simple, Moral, Accountable, Responsive, Transparent) governance.

The state must tackle the digital divide to ensure technology remains an inclusive tool for good governance.

---

## Question 68 (Year: 2022 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2022-gs4-q68-civilsdaily**

**2022 - Online methodology is being used for day-to-day meetings, institutional approvals in the administration and for teaching and learning in education sector to the extent telemedicine in the health sector is getting popular with the approvals of the competent authority. No doubt it has advantages and disadvantages for both the beneficiaries and system at large. Describe and discuss the ethical issues involved in the use of online method particularly to vulnerable section of society.** [Year: 2022] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

“Technology is a useful servant but a dangerous master.” - **Christian Lous Lange**

While online methodologies offer **paperless, and boundary-less world, they simultaneously create a **"digital wall" **of exclusion.

**Advantages and disadvantages**

| **Advantages** | **Disadvantages** |

| --- | --- |

| **Access **- eSanjeevani Telemedicine | Tribal areas lack connectivity |

| **Speed **- faster approvals | System outages. Eg- GST portal |

| **Transparency - **Eg- **Geotagging MGNREGA **assets | Data manipulation risk |

| **Continuity **- Online classes during COVID | Learning loss among rural kids |

| **Scale - **Mass service delivery. Eg- DBT | One-size-fits-all approach |

| **Efficiency - **Automation reduces delays | Errors propagate widely |

| **Flexibility **- Work-from-home | Blurs work-life boundaries |

| **Convenience - **24x7 access | Excludes **digitally illiterate** |

### Ethical issues for vulnerable sections

1.** Digital exclusion **- **“digital apartheid” **for rural students during COVID.

2.** Privacy risks **- Eg- Aadhar data breach

3.** Children **face **mental health issues **due to increased screentime, exposure to child pornography etc

4.** Informed consent erosion **- Eg- Vulnerable users often click "Agree" without understanding data-sharing terms.

5.** Surveillance concerns **-Constant AI monitoring can turn a "Welfare State" into a "Surveillance State".

6.** Difficulty in ensuring accountability **for mistakes.

7.** Loss of "Compassion" and "Conscience"- **Eg- It cannot "bend the rules" for a starving widow whose paperwork is missing.

8.** Dependency exploitation **- Eg- Middlemen charge to fill forms.

9.** Cyber fraud **- Eg- rise of digital arrest cases

10.** Cultural barriers **- Language issues in online platforms.

11.** Disability access **- Apps not accessible to visually impaired.

12.** Psychological Distress- **The "Digital Divide" causes a sense of "techno-inferiority" and alienation among the elderly and rural populations.

Online methodologies should be a **bridge, not a barrier. The way forward is not to reject technology, but to adopt a **"Phygital" (Physical + Digital) **approach.

---

## Question 69 (Year: 2024 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2024-gs4-q69-civilsdaily**

**2024 - The application of Artificial Intelligence as a dependable source of input for administrative rational decision-making is a debatable issue. Critically examine the statement from the ethical point of view.** [Year: 2024] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

The integration of AI into administration marks a shift from **"Human Discretion" **to **"Algorithmic Governance." **However, its role as a "dependable source" is **ethically complex **as "rational" decision in administration is not just about **logical consistency, but about **justice and equity.**

**Ethical Case for AI as a Dependable Source**

1. It reduces **cognitive bias **and offers **Neutrality and Objectivity **in decision making. Eg- use of AI in SSC exam evaluation

2.** Data-driven policymaking **promotes evidence-based governance. Eg- Aarogya Setu App

3.** Ensures consistency and predictability - **Eg- AI based custom approval process by DGFT

4.** Efficiency **in service delivery. Eg- **Samagra Vedika **platform of telangana create a "360-degree profile" of every citizen to verify eligibility for welfare schemes

5. By removing the **"human interface", AI reduces the opportunity for **bribery and rent-seeking. **EgAI-driven **MCA21 V3 **portal flags suspicious shell companies and fraudulent filings.

6.** Enhances accuracy. Eg- IMD using AI for weather forcasting

7.** Disaster Management Efficiency- **Eg- **Google's AI Flood Forecasting **model, used by **CWC, provides real-time flood alerts

8.** Targeted welfare delivery **- AI improves beneficiary identification in DBT.

9.** Utilitarian Optimization- Eg- NITI Aayog **partnered with IBM to develop AI models for **Crop Yield Prediction for farmers**

10. Enhancing **public participation **through **language inclusivity. Eg- **BHASHINI **platform

**Ethical Concerns**

1.** The "Black Box" Problem- **AI logic is often opaque.

2.** Institutionalizing Historical Bias- **If data is biased , the AI will "learn" and automate that bias. Eg- **US COMPAS tool biased against African-Americans.**

3.** Difficulty in ensuring accountability **for mistakes.

4.** Loss of "Compassion" and "Conscience"- **Eg- It cannot "bend the rules" for a starving widow whose paperwork is missing.

5.** Digital Dehumanization- **AI reduces complex human lives into "risk scores" or "eligibility percentages".

6.** Threat to Right to Privacy- **Constant AI monitoring can turn a "Welfare State" into a "Surveillance State".

7.** Skill Atrophy- **Administrators may stop using their own judgment, leading to a loss of critical thinking -"Steel Frame" to **"Silicon Frame"**

8. Widening **North-South divide **- Poor countries lack access to tech-mediated services.

### Way Forward- "Human-Centric AI."

1.** Explainable AI- **Implementing systems where the AI must provide a "human-readable" reason for every decision.

2.** Human-in-the-Loop (HITL)- **The final "sign-off," especially in cases affecting human rights, must be by a human officer.

3. Mandating **regular 3rd-party audits **of government algorithms to detect and "unlearn" biases.

4.** The EU AI Act Approach- "Risk-Based Framework" **where high-risk AI (policing or judiciary) face the highest level of ethical regulation.

5.** Digital Ethics Commissions **including ethicists, jurists, and technologists to oversee AI deployment in public service.

6.** Right to Appeal against AI- **Statutory rights for citizens to have an AI-driven decision reviewed by a human committee.

7.** Ethical Coding Standards- **Teaching **"Ethics by Design" **to programmers working on public infrastructure.

8. Training civil servants in **AI Literacy **under **Mission Karmayogi.

9. Strengthening **privacy safeguards under DPDP Act.**

The goal must be not AI-driven governance, but **ethically guided AI-assisted governance.

---

## Question 70 (Year: 2018 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2018-gs4-q70-civilsdaily**

**2018 - Distinguish between “Code of ethics” and “Code of conduct” with suitable examples.** [Year: 2018] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

A **Code of Ethics **is a set of moral values guiding behaviour, while a **Code of Conduct **prescribes specific rules regulating actions.

**Difference between code of conduct and code of ethics**

| **Code of Ethics** | **Code of Conduct** |

| --- | --- |

| Moral principles guiding decisions. Eg- **Judicial integrity in Supreme Court judges** | Behavioural rules regulating actions. Eg- **CCS Conduct Rules, 1964** |

| Value-oriented framework. Eg- **Medical ethics of patient confidentiality** | Rule-oriented framework. Eg- **Mandatory asset declaration by IAS officers** |

| Broad ethical ideals. Eg- **Police impartiality during communal violence** | Specific operational norms. Eg- **Election duty neutrality guidelines** |

| Encourages conscience-based actions. Eg-
**Whistleblowing against corruption** | Requires formal compliance. Eg- **Ban on accepting government gifts** |

| Flexible ethical guidance. Eg- **Compassion during disaster relief operations** | Rigid administrative instructions. Eg- **Official social media usage restrictions** |

| Self-regulatory principles. Eg- **Journalistic commitment to truthfulness** | Institutionally enforceable rules. Eg-
**Suspension for workplace harassment** |

| Focuses on “right conduct”. Eg- **Fairness in judicial verdicts** | Focuses on “allowed conduct”. Eg-
**Attendance and punctuality requirements** |

| Moral violation harms credibility. Eg- **Biased reporting by journalists** | Rule violation attracts penalties. Eg-**Dismissal for bribery charges** |

| Shapes ethical culture. Eg- **Corporate transparency and accountability values** | Maintains organisational discipline. Eg-
**Uniform code in armed forces** |

| Inspired by ideals and philosophy. Eg- **Gandhian principles in public service** | Derived from legal regulations. Eg- **Service rules for civil servants** |

### Significance of “Code of Ethics” and “Code of Conduct”

**1. Promote Integrity & Accountability**

**2. Strengthen Public Trust**

**3. Guide Ethical Decision Making**

**4. Prevent Corruption**

**5. Improve Professional Discipline**

**6. Support Good Governance**

Together, **Code of Ethics **and **Code of Conduct **create morally responsible, disciplined, and accountable institutions essential for ethical governance.

---

## Question 71 (Year: 2024 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2024-gs4-q71-civilsdaily**

**2024 - ‘The ‘Code of Conduct’ and ‘Code of Ethics’ are the sources of guidance in public administration. There is code of conduct already in operation, whereas code of ethics is not yet put in place. Suggest a suitable model for code of ethics to maintain integrity, probity and transparency in governance.** [Year: 2024] [Marks: 10]

### Answer

The CoC and CoE are complementary approaches to ensuring **institutional integrity. While Conduct Rules are primarily "negative" in nature (what not to do), **Code of Ethics **is a **"positive" **statement of values that inspires a civil servant to do the **"right thing".

**Code of conduct and code of ethics as source of guidance**

| **Code of Conduct (CoC)** | **Code of Ethics (CoE)** |

| --- | --- |

| Provide **specific rules **for conduct | Inspirational values |

| Ensures compliance and prevention of misconduct | Promotes integrity and public good |

| Tells you what is forbidden (Minimum standards) | Tells you what is ideal (Highest standards) |

| Provides for punishment against corruption | **Probity **encourages avoiding even appearance of impropriety |

| Ensures neutrality, confidentiality and accountability | **Promotes impartiality, openness and empathy** |

| Eg- Attendance rules enforce punctuality | **Eg- Professionalism promotes diligence** |

**A Suitable Model for Code of Ethics**

### Core Philosophical Values

1.** Constitutional Morality- **Prioritizing the spirit of the Constitution over individual interests.

2. Decisions must be tested against the **"Gandhian Talisman"**- how does it help the weakest?

3.** Selflessness- **Acting solely in public interest, without seeking any benefits for oneself.

4.** Probity and Integrity- **Eg- Singapore Civil Service zero-tolerance ethics policy.

5.** Objectivity- **Making choices on merit alone.

6.** Confidentiality with Responsibility. Eg- EU data ethics norms.

### Operational and Institutional Safeguards

1. Adherence to **Gandhian Talisman **and principle of **Utilitarianism **in decision making

2.** Citizen Feedback on Ethics. Eg- Estonia e-governance feedback tools.

3.** Ethical Infrastructure- Ethics Commissioner **to provide guidance on dilemmas.

4.** Reflective Practice- **Mandatory "Ethics Audits". Eg- ISO 37001 anti-bribery certification.

5.** Protection of Dissent- **"whistleblowing" should be seen as a duty, not an act of disloyalty.

6.** Conflict of Interest Registers **to prevent actual, perceived or potential CoI.

7.** Enact a Civil Services Bill- **Legally formalize the Code of Ethics ( **2nd ARC).

8.** Mission Karmayogi- **Use AI and case-study-based modules to train officials in "Moral Reasoning."

9.** Display the Code of Ethics **in all public offices to ensure public accountability

10.** Annual Ethics Declaration. Eg- US Office of Government Ethics disclosures.

11. Ensuring **transparency **through **proactive disclosure under Section 4 of RTI**

12. Asopting **"A-S-P" Model for integrity management)**

- ** Aspiration (Values)- **Eg- **Johnson & Johnson’s "Credo"**- customer as first responsibility

- ** Strictness (Compliance)- **Eg- **U.S. Office of Government Ethics **provides clear interpretations of complex ethical dilemmas.

- ** Participation- **Employees help draft the values. Eg- **Adobe's **participative culture.

By synthesizing **Nolan Principles **with **Indian Constitutional values, we can transform the "Steel Frame" into a **compassionate instrument **of public service.

---

## Question 72 (Year: 2025 | Paper: GS IV)

**Question ID: 2025-gs4-q72-civilsdaily**

**2025 - It is said that for an ethical work culture, there must be code of ethics in place in every organisation. To ensure value-based and compliance-based work culture, what suitable measures would you adopt in your work place?** [Year: 2025] [Marks: 10]

### Answer
