### Case Study 6 (Year: 2018)

Edward Snowden, a computer expert and former CIA administrator, released confidential Government documents to the press about the existence of Government surveillance programmes. According to many legal experts and the US Government, his action violated the Espionage act of 1971, which identified the leak of State secrets as an act of treason. Yet, despite the fact that he broke the law, Snowden argued that he had a moral obligation to act. He gave a justification for his “whistle blowing” by stating that he had a duty “to inform the public as to that which is done in their name and that which is done against them.” According to Snowden, the Government’s violation of privacy had to be exposed regardless of legality since more substantive issues of social action and public morality were involved here. Many agreed with Snowden. Few argued that he broke the law and compromised national security, for which he should be held accountable.

**a. **Do you agree that Snowden’s actions were ethically justified even if legally prohibited? Why or why not? Make an argument by weighing the competing values in this case.
The case of **Edward Snowden raises a profound ethical dilemma between **obedience to law and **obedience to conscience. It raises a question of whether **moral responsibility to society can justify actions that are **legally prohibited.
**Competing Values Involved

1. Rule of Law vs Moral Conscience - Legal obedience versus ethical responsibility.

2. National Security vs Individual Privacy - State safety versus civil liberties.

3. Secrecy of State vs Transparency - Classified governance versus democratic openness.

4. Public Interest vs State Interest - Citizens’ rights versus governmental authority.

5. Institutional Loyalty vs Constitutional Values - Duty to employer versus duty to society.

6. Collective Security vs Individual liberty - Surveillance for safety versus autonomy.

7. Means vs Ends - Illegality of action versus nobility of outcome.

8. Authority vs Accountability - Power of the state versus citizen oversight.
**Arguments Supporting Snowden’s Actions

1. Snowden exposed **mass surveillance, which is violating fundamental **privacy rights without informed public consent.

2. Whistleblower Ethics - exposing **systemic wrongdoing and **institutional abuse of power.

3. Snowden argued that internal mechanisms were ineffective, leaving **public disclosure as the last resort.

4. Democratic Transparency - citizens' right to know if the state is acting **against constitutional values.

5. Civil Disobedience Tradition - breaking an unjust law is ethically justified to **awaken public conscience.

6. Utilitarian Perspective - The disclosures triggered global debate and reforms on surveillance leading to recognition of the right **to privacy of citizens.

7. Proportional Response - The scale of privacy violation justified extraordinary action.
**Arguments Against Snowden’s Actions

1. Violation of Rule of Law - Ethical governance requires adherence to law. Selective disobedience risks **anarchy.

2. National Security Risks - Disclosure of classified information endangers **intelligence operations and personnel.

3. Violation of deontological ethics - Even noble ends do not automatically justify **illegal means.

4. Lack of Democratic Mandate - Snowden acted unilaterally without public or institutional authorization.

5. Undermining Trust in Institutions - Breaches weaken public trust on government

6. Precedent for Reckless Leaks - Justification could encourage irresponsible disclosures by others.

7. Legal Accountability Principle - Breaking law demands **consequences, regardless of motive.
**Ethical Evaluation - Snowden’s actions can be considered ethically justified but legally culpable

1. His **intent was not personal gain but **public good.

2. The issue involved **fundamental rights, not policy disagreement.

3. Catalyst for Institutional Reform - His actions strengthened oversight of intelligence agencies worldwide.

4. Programs he exposed were found by subsequent courts to be unconstitutional and exceeded the authority granted by Congress.
Snowden’s actions highlight the need for **stronger institutional oversight, robust whistleblower protections, and transparent governance, so individuals are not forced to choose between **silence and illegality.
